Page 4

Commentary

The Issue of the Deadline for Exchanging Silver Coins for Legal Tender

— Liu

Since the implementation of legal tender, which has not been six months, the effect has been remarkable. However, the extension period for the use of silver coins will soon expire. After this, silver loans will lose their exchange value and become dead currency. What is worrying is that people value hard currency and are accustomed to observing from various aspects such as regional transportation, credit, knowledge, etc. It is not easy to complete the reform and transition in a short period of time. If the handling is slightly improper, it will only increase people's doubts and will inevitably lead to concealment. If the ban on concealment is strict and the rewards for reporting are generous, I am afraid that corrupt officials will take advantage of the opportunity and disturb the people. The drawbacks of opening silver mines in the late Ming Dynasty can serve as a warning. Therefore, the Legislative Yuan's deliberation on the regulations on punishing acts that hinder national currency does not include the concealment of silver. Legislative member Ma Yinchu said: "Occasional concealment of a small amount of silver by the people, if it is stipulated that they should be punished, is tantamount to opening a convenient door for the police and only disturbing the people. This is one reason. Using political power to force the people to hand over silver is enough to make the people hide silver. It is only necessary to stabilize the credit of legal tender, and the people will naturally be happy to exchange their silver for legal tender. This is the second reason." This is an essential argument that deeply understands the fundamentals of governance. If the government only makes the people aware that hiding silver is a mistake and unwise, the silver will be handed over without the need for criminal persuasion.

Although the silver that has been concentrated now has not yet been exhausted from the people, the credit concept of currency among the urban population is not as biased as before, and there is no mentality of hoarding hard currency. Even if there is a small amount of hoarding, it is still the intention of "storing grain to prevent famine." As for the interior, as a result of the continuous outflow of silver over the years, paper money is used almost entirely among the people. Moreover, since disasters have been frequent and rural areas have gone bankrupt, capital has moved to cities and is mostly concentrated in banks. Even those who are accustomed to hoarding and those who have hoarded over the years must not have large amounts. Therefore, it is not difficult to give a grace period to concentrate the silver. If the ban on use is difficult to be extended again, the exchange period should not be limited. When the people are forced to use it, they will certainly feel the futility of hoarding and think of exchanging it. If they are not allowed to exchange it, it will be a loss to the people and will it be beneficial to the country? Therefore, if the door for exchanging silver coins for legal tender can be kept open and not closed, private silver will certainly continue to come.

As for the exchange procedures in the future, they are also worth studying. Otherwise, it is easy to be misunderstood as "intending to collect for the purpose of circulation or intending to transport for profit." The criminal law is in place, and the concealment of currency will cause hesitation. Therefore, it is necessary to ensure its safety. Those who exchange legal tender at local legal tender exchange agencies must not be prohibited from exchanging it locally. If there is no way to exchange it locally, they must apply to the local public agency for a certificate or passport to go to the nearest place to exchange legal tender, or use it to pay public donations and taxes and deposits. In this way, silver will not escape, and people who hoard silver will have the convenience of exchanging it successively. The top and bottom will be linked, the people will not be disturbed, and things will gather themselves.

Henan-Anhui-Suiyue Military Headquarters Stipulates Road Protection Measures

(Nanjing) The Pinghan Railway south of Zhengzhou has recently been repeatedly stolen by bandits who have removed screws and spikes, resulting in derailments. The Henan-Anhui-Suiyue Military Headquarters ordered the road protection units to solve the cases within a time limit and stipulated road protection measures, which were sent to the Ministry of Railways and the special commissioners of various districts for compliance. The Ministry of Railways transferred the order to the Pinghan-Longhai Railway for information on the 14th. (14th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Juancheng Yellow River Rises Sharply, Opening the Peach Blossom Flood's New Record

The Yellow River in the territory of Juancheng, Shandong Province, rose sharply by one meter. The water level at Lisheng Village reached 58 meters, only 6 cm lower than the highest water level during the flood season. The biggest reason for the new record of the peach blossom flood is that the riverbed is gradually silting up and the estuary is silting up. This year's flood season is still extremely worrying. The Executive Yuan ordered the Yellow River Conservancy Commission to survey the estuary and prepare for dredging. (14th Special Dispatch)

Executive Yuan Passes Regulations on Land Tax Reduction and Exemption

Appointment of Administrative Inspectors for Various Regions of Sichuan and Gansu. Dispatch of Official Shareholders and Directors to the China National Goods Bank.

(Nanjing) The Executive Yuan held its 258th regular meeting on the morning of the 14th, attended by Kong Xiangxi, Jiang Zuobin, Chen Shuren, Huang Musong, Wu Dingchang, Chen Shaokuan, Zhang Jia'ao, Zhang Qun, Wang Shijie, He Yingqin, and Liu Ruiheng, with Kong Xiangxi presiding.

Reported Matters: The Ministry of Industry requested that Article 2 of the Regulations on Commercial Officers stationed abroad be revised to classify commercial officers as follows: A. Commercial Counselors, appointed at the senior level, stationed in embassies abroad; B. Commercial Secretaries, appointed at the recommended level, stationed in embassies or legations abroad; C. Commercial Commissioners, appointed at the recommended level, stationed in important commercial ports outside the location of embassies.

Matters for Discussion: A letter from the Central Political Committee stated that its Transportation Committee had drafted four principles for promoting railway and highway connections and requested review and implementation. It was resolved to refer the matter to the Railway Department's Economic Committee for reply. Minister Kong of the Ministry of Finance and Minister Jiang of the Ministry of Interior jointly submitted a draft of the Regulations on Land Tax Reduction and Exemption, requesting approval and submission for promulgation and implementation, and requesting that the original regulations on the exemption of taxes for highway land be abolished. The resolution was passed.

Appointments and Removals: It was resolved to appoint Yu Anmin as the Administrative Inspector of the Fourth District of Sichuan Province, Li Fang as the Administrative Inspector of the Seventh District of Sichuan Province, Cheng Maoxing as the Administrative Inspector of the Ninth District of Sichuan Province, Chen Zhixue as the Administrative Inspector of the Tenth District of Sichuan Province, and Liu Yong as the Administrative Inspector of the Seventeenth District of Sichuan Province. Zhang Hengmao was appointed as the Administrative Inspector of the First District of Gansu Province, Lu Guangxu as the Administrative Inspector of the Second District of Gansu Province, Hu Baoyi as the Administrative Inspector of the Third District of Gansu Province, Fan Puzhai as the Administrative Inspector of the Fourth District of Gansu Province, Wang Yuke as the Administrative Inspector of the Fifth District of Gansu Province, Li Xuemo as the Administrative Inspector of the Sixth District of Gansu Province, and Cao Qiwen as the Administrative Inspector of the Seventh District of Gansu Province. Minister Kong of the Ministry of Finance and Minister Wu of the Ministry of Industry jointly requested the special appointment of Chen Guangfu, Chen Xing, An Zhuotang, Zhang Yichou, Chen Hong, and Sheng Pinchen as official shareholder directors of the third session of the China National Goods Bank, and Xu Xie Kang, Zhang Hancheng, Chen Yu, Wu Qiding, and Xu Jianping as official shareholder supervisors of the seventh session of the China National Goods Bank. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 14th)

(Nanjing) The draft regulations for Zhejiang's 60 million yuan new public bond have been reviewed and completed by the Executive Yuan and have been included in the agenda, ready for discussion. On the 14th, a telegram was temporarily received from Chairman Huang, requesting a delay in the discussion, so it was decided to postpone it. It is said that the reason for the postponement is that the interest rate is still under consideration. (Special dispatch on the 14th) The Executive Yuan passed the unified regulations on land tax reduction and exemption in twenty-two articles at a meeting on the 14th. The content includes that all public land is exempt from tax, private schools and academic institutions, parks, sports fields, farms, and hospitals are eligible for a 50% reduction or exemption, and charitable organizations with achievements can apply for reduction or exemption. Surtaxes on field taxes are also reduced or exempted accordingly. (Special dispatch on the 14th)

(Nanjing) At the Executive Yuan's regular meeting on the morning of the 14th, the regulations on land tax reduction and exemption were passed. The key points are: Reduction and Exemption Standards: (A) Registered private schools and academic institutions with achievements are exempt from tax; registered private organizations and public sports fields are appropriately reduced in tax; (B) Registered agricultural and forestry experimental farms with more than ten years of achievements are appropriately reduced in tax; (C) Public hospitals with more than five years of achievements are appropriately reduced in tax; (D) Registered charitable organizations with achievements are exempt from tax; (E) Public cemeteries are exempt from tax; (F) Privately operated railways and highways are reduced or exempted from tax; (G) Disaster-stricken areas are appropriately reduced or exempted from tax. Reduction and Exemption Procedures: A. When public or private land becomes public, the competent authority shall submit it to the Ministries of Interior and Finance for joint verification and submission for exemption; B. Those requesting reduction or exemption shall submit an application to the county or city government, indicating the amount of tax, and submit it to the Ministries of Interior and Finance for approval; C. Land tax reduction or exemption due to the adjustment of social and economic conditions shall be reported by the county or city government to the Ministries of Interior and Finance for verification and submission for approval. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 14th)

(Nanjing) The Transportation Committee of the Central Political Committee has prepared a proposal to promote the connection between railways and highways. The proposal was passed at the Executive Yuan meeting on the morning of the 14th. The proposal includes the following measures: The national highway administrative authority should belong to the Ministry of Railways. The ministry should quickly draw and publish a general map of railways and highways. The national land transportation network should facilitate the mutual use of highways and railways, each maximizing its benefits, and the competent authorities should consider and handle this. To avoid competition between the two, all facilities should be properly planned by the Ministry of Railways. Uniform standards should be established for highways, bridges, and automobile construction. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 14th)

Sino-Japanese Wireless Telegraph Test Achieves Excellent Results

(Tianjin) For Sino-Japanese wireless telegraph communication, the Ministry of Communications has newly purchased two transmitting and receiving machines, one with a wavelength of 60 meters and one with a wavelength of 24 meters. They have now been installed and commissioned. Tests were conducted on the 9th, 11th, and 14th, with clear sound and good results. Formal communication is scheduled to begin on May 1st. The proposed rate for future telegrams is 8.5 jiao per word, compared to the previous rate of 1.45 yuan per word, representing a reduction of 5.7 jiao per word for formal communication. The Ministry of Communications has transferred 15 telegraph operators from Qingdao. Before implementation, two matters remain to be decided by the Ministry of Communications and the Japanese side: the issue of telegram rates and the issue of telegram rate division. (Special dispatch on the 14th)

This Week's International Conference in Geneva: Focus on European Peace or War; Discussion of Italian Issue, Conflicting Opinions Between Britain and France; Attention on the Rhineland, Concern on the Nile; Collective Security Likely to Become a Dream

Geneva The following agenda items relate to the discussion of European peace or war this week: On Tuesday, the Chairman of the Committee of Thirteen, Spanish representative Madariaga, will exchange conditions for a peace agreement on the East African issue with representatives of Italy and Abyssinia on behalf of the Committee. On Wednesday, the general staffs of Britain, France, and Belgium will meet in London to discuss joint land, air, and sea defense methods in the event of a German attack on the three countries. On Thursday, the Committee of Thirteen will hear Madariaga's report. Unless Italy can accept a fair peace proposal, the League of Nations will be required to impose new sanctions on Italy. This step will inevitably lead to two natural consequences: either a head-on conflict due to conflicting opinions between Britain and France, or Italy's inevitable revenge against Britain, deepening the war crisis in the Mediterranean. However, Britain will do its best to deal with both consequences, first because the British public is outraged by Italy's inhumane air bombings and the use of poison gas, and the government must take this into account; second, the British government can no longer ignore Mussolini's ambitions in East Africa and the Mediterranean.

Today, someone here made a very insightful criticism of the current stalemate, saying, "If France only focuses on the Rhine and Britain only cares about the Nile, then the so-called collective security will forever become a beautiful dream for mere talk." (National Telegram on the 13th)

Pro-British or Pro-Italian: France Hesitates on the Wrong Path

Premier Sarraut to Deliver Speech Explaining Position on the Italian-Abyssinian Case

(Paris) Whether France will adopt a pro-Italian policy or a pro-British policy when the Committee of Thirteen meets on Thursday is causing French politicians to rack their brains. Premier Sarraut met with Italian Ambassador to France Cerutti today. Afterwards, according to a spokesperson from official circles, France's attitude will not be determined before the British cabinet meeting on Tuesday. At the same time, Sarraut will also consult with Peng Gu. The Paris Afternoon News commented on the current situation as follows: "Today, the divergence of opinions between Britain and France will not only destroy British-French cooperation in Europe, but will also disintegrate the League of Nations." Former Premier Laval, who has remained silent since resigning, also spoke out today, advocating that France quickly reach an understanding with Germany. He believes that there is no benefit in simply refusing to negotiate. At the same time, Laval also advocated lifting sanctions against Italy to fully restore its participation in European affairs. Finally, Laval expressed indignation at Britain's tolerance of German rearmament. (National Telegram on the 13th)

(Paris) Premier Sarraut received Italian Ambassador Cerutti in the afternoon at 6:30 and did not finish the meeting until 8:00. The Premier immediately went to the Presidential Palace to meet with President Lebrun to report on the conversation. It is said that Cerutti asked the Premier what attitude the French government would take on the Italian-Abyssinian peace issue. Foreign Minister Flandin, who had gone to the countryside for the Easter holidays, recently notified Premier Sarraut that he would return to the capital on Wednesday (the 15th). The Premier has scheduled to deliver an important political speech on that day, broadcast by radio. At that time, all national radio stations will suspend broadcasting political speeches made by others. (Havas dispatch on the 13th)

No Understanding Between Germany and France: European Peace Difficult to Achieve

Laval Reiterates Former Policy: Advocates Restoring the Stresa Front

Clermont-Ferrand, France Former Premier and Foreign Minister Laval recently gave an interview to a reporter from a local newspaper, saying, "If there is no compromise between Germany and France, then European peace cannot be achieved." When I was Premier and Foreign Minister, I tried in many ways to bring Germany and France closer together. However, Germany repaid France's compromise attempts by abolishing the Locarno Treaty. France had previously requested Germany to join the Eastern European Pact. At that time, German Foreign Minister Neurath declared that even if other countries agreed on mutual assistance measures, Germany was also prepared to join the Eastern European Pact, provided that they were listed in individual documents. Who knew that after Russia and France concluded a mutual assistance pact, German Führer Hitler used this as an excuse to abolish the Locarno Treaty? I do not want to hinder the actions of the current French government. "Although I do not want to consider the details of the specific suggestions already put forward by Hitler, I believe that it is a mistake for France to stubbornly adhere to its prejudices and refuse to negotiate. Today, the unease in people's hearts and the chaos in the situation can be said to permeate the whole of Europe. Those in power should act quickly and decisively to resolve all outstanding issues between Germany and France as soon as possible." Laval then recalled his policy on the Italian-Abyssinian dispute when he was in office, saying that if Britain and France could understand each other, they could cooperate seamlessly. When I parted ways with British Foreign Secretary Sir Hoare in Paris at the end of last year (after drafting the Italian-Abyssinian peace plan), I declared that if our compromise policy was successful, the international situation would be clear. In the future, we can find ways to bring Germany into the ranks of collective security organizations. Unfortunately, peace in East Africa has not been restored, and peace in Europe is still awaiting creation. What are we doing now? On the one hand, we are invoking the Locarno Treaty and asking Italy to cooperate fully. On the other hand, we are fulfilling the League of Nations Covenant and continuing to impose sanctions on Italy. How can we allow this contradiction to persist? We should now restore the British-French-Italian front created by the Stresa Conference and lift the sanctions to allow the Italian-Abyssinian peace agreement to be concluded. Only then can we look at the fate of Europe with greater confidence, and the organization of the peace mechanism will also be somewhat promising." (Havas dispatch on the 12th)

British Government Does Not Want to Intensify Sanctions Against Italy

Eden Scheduled to Go to Geneva Today: Plans to Strive to Find a Solution

(London) According to people here, the British government does not intend to intensify sanctions against Italy at this time. Although the sub-committee of eighteen nations of the League of Nations General Assembly will be convened soon, its purpose is not to discuss intensifying sanctions, but only to review the implementation of the current sanctions. These people also said that Italian-Abyssinian peace negotiations will begin in Geneva in the near future, and the British government sincerely hopes that it will be successful. (Havas dispatch on the 13th)

(London) Rumors say that because economic sanctions are insufficient to end the Italian-Abyssinian War, Britain intends to implement military sanctions. Other important member states of the League of Nations are also prepared to support Britain in taking this action. The public was alarmed by this news. However, according to well-informed sources, this rumor is completely unfounded. The British government's policy has not changed. The Paris community also does not believe it. According to the French Foreign Ministry, only the Committee of Eighteen Nations can decide whether the League of Nations should impose military sanctions on Italy. French political circles believe that British Foreign Secretary Eden and French Foreign Minister Flandin will never discuss military action. No such rumors have been heard in Geneva, and the claim that important member states of the League of Nations guarantee to support Britain in taking military action is not believed. Geneva now feels that any new sanctions that are more effective will cause very serious controversy. (Reuters dispatch on the 14th)

(London) Foreign Secretary Eden recently returned to the capital from the countryside this afternoon and is scheduled to go to Geneva in the afternoon tomorrow to attend the meeting of the Committee of Thirteen of the Executive Yuan of the League of Nations. He will also discuss everything with Prime Minister Baldwin at Sassoon's villa in Trent Park tonight. According to responsible sources, the main task of the British representative is to seek a solution to the Italian-Abyssinian dispute. However, it is not allowed to express what position Britain should take if mediation fails. As for Germany, no contact will be made before the end of this week. British Ambassador to Germany Sir Phipps has not yet received any instructions. (Havas dispatch on the 14th)

Italy Sends Personnel to Geneva to Discuss Peace Issues

Meeting of the Committee of Thirteen Postponed

Geneva Italian Prime Minister's confidential secretary Alocchi will discuss the peace issues between Italy and Abyssinia with Madariaga, Chairman of the Committee of Thirteen of the Executive Yuan of the League of Nations. A telegram from Rome said that he would arrive in Geneva no earlier than Wednesday afternoon. Madariaga will also meet with the Abyssinian representative, Abyssinian Minister to France Huater, beforehand. (Havas Agency dispatch on the 14th)

(Rome) The government has recently decided to appoint Alocchi as its representative to discuss the Italian-Abyssinian peace negotiations with the chairman of the Committee of Thirteen. Political figures here believe that the current dispute is not between Italy and the League of Nations, but between Britain and Italy. British Foreign Secretary Eden has recently been collecting materials on the Italian military's methods of warfare in order to accuse Italy and provide an excuse for intensifying sanctions. Although Italy will fully respect Britain's interests, it will do its best to protect all its own interests and resist any threats. (Havas dispatch on the 13th)

(Rome) Political figures recently said that Italy wants to directly and completely control Abyssinia, and no matter how Britain and the League of Nations resist, they will not be able to contain the power of the Fascist Party. Although military conflict between Britain and Italy is unlikely, if Britain attacks Italy with force, Italy will be able to deal with it easily. (Havas dispatch on the 14th)

Following Diplomatic Channels: Britain and Germany Continue Negotiations

Eden's Visit to Berlin Unconfirmed

(London) Foreign Secretary Eden is currently in the countryside for the Easter holidays and is scheduled to return to the capital tomorrow. According to inquiries from this agency's reporters, the British government has now decided to continue negotiations with Germany through diplomatic channels. Foreign Secretary Eden himself will not go to Berlin to meet with Führer Hitler. Regarding these negotiations, the government will soon order British Ambassador to Germany Sir Phipps to raise questions with the German government regarding several points in the German memorandum. At that time, the British government will decide its attitude based on the German government's response. (Havas dispatch on the 13th)

Britain to Propose Suggestions: Reconciling French and German Plans

Peace in Central and Eastern Europe Urgently Needs to be Maintained. Conclusion of Non-Aggression Pact within the Scope of the League of Nations.

(London) As far as people know, the British government urgently wants to maintain peace in Eastern and Central Europe. It will soon make suggestions to Germany to reconcile the peace plans of France and Germany. Generally speaking, Britain advocates that the mutual non-aggression treaties proposed by Germany should be regularly included in the mutual assistance clauses, and that the obligations undertaken by each country that signs this treaty should take precedence over those stipulated in the League of Nations Covenant, and that the others should be determined so as to be compatible with the alliance and also harmonize with France's suggestions. Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov had previously raised an objection, saying that according to the method proposed by Germany, if Germany invaded another country, the countries that had signed a non-aggression treaty with Germany would not be able to fulfill the mutual assistance obligations contained in the League of Nations Covenant. If mutual assistance clauses are included in the non-aggression treaty, then the Soviet Union's objection cannot be established. (Havas dispatch on the 13th)

Anglo-French-Belgian General Staff Talks Begin Today

(London) The talks that the general staffs of Britain, France, and Belgium should conduct in accordance with the draft Locarno Treaty are scheduled to begin tomorrow (Tuesday). The Italian government has not yet ratified this agreement and will not send personnel to participate. The Belgian general staff is represented by Lieutenant General Terfonton and Major Waters (military attaché at the British embassy). (Havas dispatch on the 14th)

(Rome) According to responsible sources here, the Locarno Treaty countries will hold military talks and have asked Italy to send a representative to participate. However, the Italian government has not yet decided whether to participate. (Reuters dispatch on the 13th)

Rome Claims: Italian Troops Occupy Dessie

News Not Confirmed: Aircraft Scatter Leaflets Over Addis Ababa

(Rome) According to news here, Dessie has been occupied by Italian motorized troops without any resistance. Mussolini, in order to eliminate Abyssinia's last resistance, has ordered the Italian troops on the northern route to hasten their advance towards Addis Ababa. According to Italian speculation, the fall of Addis Ababa will not be more than two or three weeks away. According to diplomatic circles in Addis Ababa, Mussolini may force the Emperor of Abyssinia to abdicate and support Duke Hara as a puppet. If the Emperor of Abyssinia resists further, the Italian army will occupy Addis Ababa. (National Telegram on the 13th)

(Rome) The claim that Italian troops have occupied Dessie has not been confirmed by official circles. However, according to reliable sources, Italian troops are currently working hard to attack, hoping to capture it by the Roman birth festival on April 21. If the Italian army occupies Dessie or Harar, General Graziani, commander-in-chief of the Italian army on the southern route, will begin his attack on Addis Ababa. General Badoglio, commander-in-chief of the Italian army in East Africa, congratulated war correspondents on Easter, telling them that they would soon have a lot of work to do. At the same time, the whereabouts of the King of Abyssinia remain a mystery. Some say that he has cut off his beard and fled to avoid being recognized and attacked by the tribal people, some say that he will abdicate sooner or later, and some say that Italy intends to use Duke Harar as a puppet king. However, none of these claims can be confirmed. (Reuters dispatch on the 14th)

Asmara Ten Italian bombers flew south from Magal, a city in northern Abyssinia, along the Dessie Road yesterday, and met with nine reconnaissance planes south of Dessie. They circled several times over Addis Ababa but did not drop bombs. They only dropped leaflets saying that the army led by the Emperor of Abyssinia had been destroyed and that the Italian army was here to abolish slavery and introduce modern civilization. The Kwantung Army and Japanese imperialists are all aware that Manchuria is in turmoil everywhere, and that the "liberated" Manchurian and Mongolian people are storing up all sorts of monstrous things for them. Pan-American Peace Conference

To Be Convened in Washington Today; Representatives from Twenty-One Countries to Attend

(Washington) Representatives from twenty-one countries in North and South America will meet here on Tuesday to discuss preliminary plans for a Western Hemisphere peace conference. US Government Plan

(Washington) The government will submit a plan to the Preparatory Committee of the Pan-American Peace Conference for review. The main points are no more than the following four items:

The countries of the Americas implement a tariff truce.

Any country in the Americas that has an act of aggression will be subject to economic sanctions by other countries.

Establish a permanent security system to protect American peace.

All related countries act in unison to maintain neutrality in the European war. Regarding the first item, Secretary of State Hull attaches the most importance to it, wanting to set a period of five years during which the related countries must not raise tariff rates. Regarding the second item, American public opinion has always been extremely opposed to the economic sanctions decided by the League of Nations. The government is not unaware of this, but believes that the economic sanctions decided by the League of Nations are European sanctions, which are very different from the cooperation of American countries to deal with those who disturb the peace of the Americas. State Department officials also declared that the above four items are only suggestions and can be used as the basis for discussion. Once all related countries unanimously agree, they should be submitted to the Pan-American Peace Conference. (Havas 電, 13th)

Roosevelt's Campaign Speech: Continuing to Strive to Restore Prosperity

Still Advancing Towards the Economic Goals of the New Deal; Six Ways to Reduce Domestic Unemployment

Baltimore President Roosevelt delivered a broadcast speech from the Maryland Young Democrats tonight, informing the whole country that this was his first decisive statement to begin his re-election campaign, declaring that he would continue to strive for social progress. He would reconsider shorter work weeks and adequate minimum wages, and the reduction of the number of unemployed people each year. President Roosevelt said that social work has only just begun. Although production increased and profits were higher in 1928 and 1929, the number of unemployed people increased rapidly to an alarming extent. Therefore, merely wanting to restore what ordinary people call a state of prosperity is of no use. Now, while restoring prosperity, we must also reduce unemployment. There are six ways to do this:

Expand purchasing power and distribute it more widely.

Raise the age at which children leave school.

Have older workers retire and give them pensions.

Shorten weekly working hours.

Distribute employment evenly throughout the year.

Provide an adequate minimum wage. President Roosevelt's remarks indicate that even though he has suffered setbacks, he still wants to pursue policies similar to the National Recovery Act. (Reuters, 13th)

External Consolidation: Staff of Overseas Embassies and Consulates

A Special Qualification Review Committee is Established with Chen Jie as the Chairman; Emphasizing Virtue, Learning, Writing, Appearance, and Physical Fitness; Recruiting Real Talent

(Nanjing) In order to carefully select staff for overseas embassies and consulates and to consolidate the diplomatic ranks, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has established a Qualification Review Committee for Staff of Overseas Embassies and Consulates. On the 14th, it announced that Chen Jie would be the Chairman, and Tan Shaohua, Lin Chunxian, Wu Songgao, Liu Shishun, Gao Zongwu, and Li Dijun would be the committee members. In the future, personnel assigned to overseas posts, in addition to being handled in accordance with the Law on the Appointment of Civil Servants, their qualifications should first be strictly reviewed by the committee in accordance with regulations. According to a certain authority in the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, since Minister Zhang took office, he has spared no effort in adjusting the Ministry's structure and personnel. The performance evaluation within the Ministry has been completed, and the personnel of various overseas missions will also be actively consolidated. Because the staff of overseas embassies and consulates are representatives of the country, they bear a heavy responsibility. In addition to possessing the qualifications that ordinary civil servants should have, special attention must be paid to the following five words: "Virtue," "Learning," "Writing," "Appearance," and "Physical Fitness." Virtue should be pure, learning should be refined, writing should be proficient, appearance should be dignified, and physical fitness should be strong. If one has the legal qualifications of an ordinary civil servant and also possesses these five qualities, then going to other countries will enhance the glory of the country and gain the good reputation of foreigners. Now our country pays attention to the rule of law and strives to guarantee rights. But since we want to talk about guarantees, we must first carefully select officials for appointment. Since the qualifications required for embassy and consular personnel are different from those of ordinary civil servants, when appointing embassy and consular personnel, in addition to the standards stipulated in the Law on the Appointment of Civil Servants, one must also consider these factors as the goal and be especially careful. Moreover, since the opinion of a single senior official in the Ministry may not be comprehensive, the method of a committee has been specially adopted in order to pool ideas and benefit from each other. Although the Ministry had previously promulgated the "Provisional Regulations for the Qualification Review Committee for Diplomatic and Consular Officials," it has not yet been established. In order to implement it thoroughly, the existing regulations have been revised and formulated as the Provisional Regulations for the Qualification Review Committee for Staff of Overseas Embassies and Consulates of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, which was promulgated on the 10th. The Permanent Vice Minister serves as one of the committee members, and six senior officials of the Ministry serve as committee members. The qualifications of all personnel in overseas embassies and consulates, other than ambassadors and ministers, regardless of the transfer of existing personnel or the dispatch of newly appointed personnel, must first be carefully reviewed by the committee. The criteria for review, in addition to being handled in accordance with the provisions of general laws and regulations, will also take into account the above-mentioned five words: "Virtue," "Learning," "Writing," "Appearance," and "Physical Fitness," so as to prevent redundancy, recruit good talents, and promote the fame of outstanding individuals at home and abroad. In addition, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs issued an order saying that employing people based on talent has been a clear lesson since ancient times. In the way of selecting talent, qualifications come first. The staff of overseas embassies and consulates represent the country, promote friendly relations, and protect overseas Chinese affairs. With regard to the selection of personnel, how should we carefully select them to be appropriate? However, the law has been lax for many years, and the appointment has been redundant. In order to prevent opportunism and recruit real talents, the Ministry has specially established a Qualification Review Committee for Staff of Overseas Embassies and Consulates to specialize in review. In the future, personnel assigned to overseas posts by the Ministry, in addition to complying with the Law on the Appointment of Civil Servants, their qualifications should first be strictly examined in accordance with the newly formulated regulations. Virtue and learning must be excellent, language skills must be refined, appearance and physical fitness must be emphasized, and compatibility between people and places is especially important. In this way, outstanding individuals can be promoted and used in all directions, without deviating from the fundamental purpose of the country in employing people. There is high hope for this. This order. (Central News Agency, 14th)

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has established a Qualification Review Committee for Staff of Overseas Embassies and Consulates. After the Provisional Regulations are promulgated by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Minister Zhang will appoint Chen Jie as the Chairman of the Qualification Review Committee for Staff of Overseas Embassies and Consulates, and Tan Shaohua, Lin Chunxian, Wu Songgao, Liu Shishun, Gao Zongwu, and Li Dijun as committee members. Qian Yi, the head of the Records Section of the General Affairs Department, also serves as the secretary. It was officially established on the 14th. From that day on, the list of existing consuls-general, consuls, vice-consuls, and staff members of overseas missions will be collected and reviewed by the Records Section. If there are those who are not suitable for the place or whose virtue and learning are not very rich, they will be transferred separately. In the future, all Ministry orders announcing embassy and consular personnel must first be reviewed and approved by the committee before they can take office. The first meeting will be held within days, and eight regulations will be announced. (Special Telegram, 14th)

Dr. He Lian Publishes: Insight into Financial Problems

(Nanjing) Economic expert He Lian recently came to Nanjing after completing his inspection in Sichuan. The reporter, because Mr. He is not only a famous economist in our country, but has also conducted on-the-spot inspections of the economy of various provinces, specially visited him to ask for his opinion on the financial problems in the extraordinary period when economic circles are hotly debating. He answered in great detail. Mr. He advocated that we should take advantage of the enthusiastic psychology of the people across the country in preparing for financial problems in the extraordinary period to seek the soundness of our country's tax system, thereby establishing a solid foundation for finance in the extraordinary period. Mr. He believes that a sound tax system is indeed the only way for our country to achieve self-reliance, and it is also a more reliable way to enrich financial revenue in the extraordinary period. Because most of our country's current taxes are indirect taxes, they will change during the extraordinary period. If direct taxes are gradually implemented, they can not only meet the financial needs of the extraordinary period, but also conform to the spirit of modern tax systems. Mr. He also advocated that among direct taxes, income tax and inheritance tax should be implemented first. Someone said that our country's socio-economic situation is still in the state of the Middle Ages, and it is not suitable to implement modern tax systems. He replied that our country cannot stick to the old ways and not cater to the spirit of modern tax systems. Others said that the revenue from direct taxes in the future, during the extraordinary period, may not be sufficient to offset the shortfall in indirect taxes. He replied that if the implementation of direct taxes falls into an extraordinary state at the beginning, of course there will be no tax revenue. If it has a considerable history, even if we only talk about income tax, it will definitely not be limited to the revenue of 5 million yuan set in the national budget for the 24th year. Finally, Mr. He hoped that the government should pay attention to three things when implementing direct taxes: The legislation must be simple. Initially, it can be handled concurrently by other financial institutions. It should be promoted in stages. (Central News Agency, 14th)

Tiger Scare in Hong Kong; British Naval Officers Get Lost Hiking and Encounter Two Tigers

Frightened, the tigers left them alone.

(Hong Kong) Two British naval officers were hiking in Tai Mo Shan (transliteration) yesterday with a climbing group. They got lost in the nearby mountains and were unable to find their way out by dusk, wandering in the mountains all night. Suddenly, they encountered two tigers as large as oxen. Neither officer was armed. Fortunately, the tigers left them alone, but the two officers were greatly frightened. After returning from the mountains, they told others about the incident. Because tigers have frequently been seen in the mountains recently, everyone is taking precautions. It is reported that a Chinese woman who was cutting grass has gone missing and is presumed to have been eaten by tigers. It is expected that the police will join with local villagers in the area to organize a hunting party to eliminate the tiger threat. (14th day Reuters dispatch)

Predicting that the Yellow River Will Not Pose a Threat This Year Despite High Water

— Kong Xiangrong's Conversation in Xuzhou —

(Xuzhou) Kong Xiangrong passed through Xuzhou today en route from Bian to Beijing, reporting on the Dongzhuang closure. Kong stated that the dyke closure project cost over 2 million yuan, saving about 1 million yuan compared to the budget. A Yellow River conference was held in Bian, deciding to continue fortifying dangerous sections of the dyke to ensure its long-term stability. It is predicted that the Yellow River will not pose a threat this year despite high water levels, but unified command over the entire Yellow River is necessary to effectively prevent future risks and benefit from its resources. (14th day special dispatch)

The Seventeen Kings of Kawa Advocate Using the Salween River as the Yunnan-Burma Border; Issue an Open Letter to Compatriots Calling for Unified Advocacy; And Write to Neutral Commissioner Ehlers

Kunming Correspondence: The Yunnan Provincial Guomindang Steering Committee received a letter yesterday from the Kawa Seventeen Kings Tribal People's Council, requesting assistance in the Yunnan-Burma border survey, advocating the use of the southern section of the Salween River as the natural boundary, and attaching the Kawa Seventeen Kings' Open Letter to Compatriots and a letter to neutral commissioner Mr. Ehlers. The committee copied the attached documents and submitted them to the Provincial Government for review and handling. This matter concerns the border region peoples' self-determination regarding border demarcation. The Open Letter to Compatriots and the letter to Mr. Ehlers are recorded below:

Open Letter to Compatriots

We, the Kawa Seventeen Kings region, border Shuangjiang and Lancang to the east, Mengliang to the south, the lower reaches of the Salween River to the west, and Keqian and Mengding to the north. Since ancient times, our ancestors have been enfeoffed by the Chinese Emperor to guard the frontier for thousands of years. This is not only recorded in history books, but also evidenced by seals issued by successive dynasties. Although we, the Kawa people, are from the uncivilized frontier of Yunnan and have not received the benefits of Chinese culture and education, our languages and scripts are different, yet our men diligently cultivate the land, and our women focus on weaving, working day and night to support ourselves, which is largely the same as the Han people. Due to the dangers of the high mountains and the isolation caused by miasma and rain, travel is fraught with fear, leading to distance and separation from our motherland. This is the general situation of the division between the uncivilized and the civilized. Since the loss of Burma, and our motherland has faced many difficulties over the years, British imperialists have taken advantage of their management of Burma to advance into the north and south Yi mountains, and even send troops across the river. They have dispatched over a thousand soldiers, equipped with modern weapons, ostensibly to explore and investigate mines, blinding and deafening our motherland, and confounding the world's sense of justice. They have secretly occupied our Banghong, Honglufang, and other mining areas to satisfy their ambitious aggression, disregarding the League of Nations treaties, and using all means to oppress us, wanting to obtain our Kawa land and enslave our Kawa people to achieve their goals. Alas, we Kawa people are simple and unsophisticated, without any prior planning, how can we defend against the comprehensive plan of a civilized world power for decades? How can bows, arrows, and matchlocks defend against modern weapons? Helpless, we can only wait for our demise, losing our land and being exterminated, which is imminent. Alas, we are responsible for protecting the land passed down by our ancestors, but we will lose it, and our descendants will not inherit it from us. We cannot face our ancestors in the afterlife, and what can we say to future generations? We kings should have planned long ago, sacrificing sleep and food, gathering together to discuss and swear oaths. Although Kawa is small and its people weak, it has thousands of square miles of land and hundreds of thousands of people. Relying on the natural barriers and our inherent bravery, we vow to cut off our heads rather than lose our duty to defend our land, and shed our blood rather than become colonial slaves. Even if we have only one gun and one bullet, one woman and one child, we will break our bodies but never change our hearts. From now on, we will rely on the spirit of self-determination and self-defense, and the resolve to die to live, not fearing the invasion of powerful enemies' ambitions. Our Kawa land is the extreme western frontier of China's national defense, and is the western and southern part of China. Its gain or loss is important and relates to the security of the motherland, especially Yunnan, Sichuan, and Guizhou provinces. How can we not be in danger? Moreover, the Kawa region is rich in gold and silver, renowned throughout the world. British imperialists have long coveted it, taking advantage of our motherland's troubled times to boldly send troops and establish camps, intending to occupy it permanently. At this time of border survey, if we do not forcefully argue and reclaim our land, it would be no different than handing over our treasures to the enemy, and handing over the entire Kawa nation to imperialists as a tool to suppress other small and weak nations. Our motherland's government is forced to endure and concede. We Kawa people, although foolish, are determined not to willingly submit and allow ourselves to be driven and divided as slaves of British colonialism, giving up this precious and useful territory. Furthermore, the Kawa region borders the Salween River to the west. Since ancient times, our ancestors have lived here, relying on the river as a natural boundary. The customs and habits of the people are not much different from those of China. We kings believe that this border survey should be based on the boundaries familiar to the local people as recorded in the former Yunnan-Burma treaty, and also the envoy's note should be based on the terrain relevant to the issue, which is the fundamental way to resolve disputes in the border survey. What is more familiar to the local people than our Kawa kings' ancestral homeland seals, and the determination to use the river as the boundary? Considering that our government officials may be weak and follow precedents, willing to satiate the imperialists' greed with our Kawa land and people, we dare to convene the Kawa Tribal People's Self-Determination Representative Assembly in Gansai, and publicly elect representatives to collect seals and evidence, and plead with the border surveyors to state the Kawa people's pain and vow not to be slaves or beasts of burden, requesting our border survey team to forcefully argue based on this. Although it is uncertain whether we can fully achieve our goal, we Kawa people recall the early oaths and the gradual announcement of the self-determination and unity policy to heaven and earth. We vow to cut off our heads rather than be colonial slaves. Therefore, we respectfully inform our government, provincial officials, legal groups, and compatriots, as well as neighboring county magistrates and government offices, overseas compatriots, elders, brothers, sisters, asking you to have compassion on the suffering and helplessness of our small border nation, to remember the fear of lip loss and teeth chill, and the danger of scraping rice to see the kernel, and to provide practical assistance directly or indirectly, or to write requests to widely inform our national compatriots, so that the Kawa people can achieve self-determination, self-defense, and the preservation of our national territory, and not suffer the fate of being subjugated like the Burmese. Then the border people will be fortunate, and the national defense will also be fortunate. Respectfully, the Kawa Seventeen Kings.

Letter to Mr. Ehlers

Mr. Ehlers, Chairman of the Sino-British Border Survey Committee, we respectfully express our most sincere trust and heartfelt wishes to you. You, entrusted by the League of Nations to resolve the border disputes in the southern section of the Yunnan-Burma border, have come from afar. Your position is the position of the League of Nations, and your glory is the glory of the League of Nations. We are deeply gratified to see your arrival, like seeing light in a dark room. Previously, China lost Burma, but the British were not satisfied and wanted to obtain our Wa land. We believe that Wa land is China's border area, and the Wa people are a part of the Chinese nation. We also have seals issued by the Han Emperor as evidence. Our customs and habits are largely the same. We are all part of the same body and do not want to be divided. We also have a duty to defend our land, so how can we give up? Therefore, we have always been united, preventing the British from advancing even one step on the border line. This is why the Yunnan-Burma border issue has been unresolved for so long. Now, you are presiding over public deliberation, resolving doubts and analyzing disputes. May your wisdom shine brightly and without concealment.

We respectfully request that you, based on our inherent territory, with the spirit of fearlessness and the means to quickly resolve disputes, resolutely advocate that this section should use the Salween River as the natural boundary, then the disputes can be resolved, the people's hearts can be satisfied, the tragedy of bloodshed can be avoided, and your noble benevolence can shine with the sun and moon. In recent times, the self-determination of the Saar people has been praised throughout the ages. Although the Wa land is small, we admire justice. We believe that Great Britain, with its vast territory and wealth, has already gained much and should not abandon the friendship between the two countries for this small area, nor mobilize troops to oppress our helpless and weak nation, which would be ridiculed by the world. If not, entering our borders, invading our territory, enslaving our people, and forcefully seizing our territory, then we Wa people, although foolish, will also exhaust our knowledge and ability to carry out legitimate defense. We may break our bodies, but we will never change our hearts. Even if we have only one gun and one bullet, one woman and one child, we will fight to the end and never willingly submit and be slaughtered, bringing indelible shame to the Chinese nation. Now, at the time of the Sino-British border survey, we have gathered in Gansai and decided to hire Mr. Yin Peiyun, a resident of Gansai in Wa land, as our plenipotentiary representative to lead us to attend. We believe that you, with your foresight, will be able to understand the key to this problem. We dare to inform you of our humble intentions, hoping that you will consider them and forward them to the General Assembly of the League of Nations in Geneva. (Central News Agency)

Guangdong Province Emphasizes Local Autonomy, Reduces Public Security Sub-Bureaus, and Merges Them with District and Township Offices

Guangzhou Correspondence: The Civil Affairs Department of Guangdong Province has strongly promoted local autonomy in recent years. District and township offices have been fully established throughout the province. In order to implement the spirit of autonomy, save local finances, and reduce the burden on the people, it has been decided to gradually transfer local public security matters to autonomous organizations. Currently, the province has 422 public security sub-bureaus, 150 stationed posts, and 45 police stations in various counties. After considering the local environment, a large portion will be reduced and merged with district and township offices. Only 150 public security sub-bureaus will be temporarily retained. The order was issued to various locations in the middle of last month for strict implementation. The detailed implementation measures are divided into fourteen articles, which are extracted as follows:

* The public security sub-bureaus that have been approved for retention should all be renamed as "口口 County Public Security Bureau 口口 Sub-bureau" with the name of the location prefixed. The area under their jurisdiction will be re-approved by the county government and a map will be drawn and submitted to the Civil Affairs Department for record.

* The public security sub-bureaus that have been approved for retention should resubmit their staffing table and revenue and expenditure budget to the Civil Affairs Department for review.

* If a portion of the funding for the public security sub-bureaus that have been approved for retention is shared by townships, a portion of the funds should be allocated to the district office as autonomous funding.

* All public security sub-bureaus that have not been approved for retention will be abolished. From now on, public security matters in each district will be handled by the district offices.

* The abolished public security bureaus and posts should immediately prepare a detailed list of documents, equipment, firearms, and income items, and submit it to the county government for verification and transfer to the district office. The seals should be returned and cancelled.

* The abolished public security bureaus and posts may be granted gratuities and pensions.

* The original income of the abolished public security bureaus and posts that is deemed to be exploitative should be reduced or exempted to reduce the burden on the people.

* The number of police officers to be established in the district office should be approved by the county government based on local needs and reported to the Civil Affairs Department for record.

* If the number of police officers in the district office is [unclear] or more, a chief should be established. If the number exceeds ten, the number of chiefs may be appropriately increased.

* If the number of [unclear] in the district office is ten or more, a patrol officer should be established to assist the district chief in handling public security matters.

* The officers will be [unclear] by the county government.

* The district office police should all be graduates of the Guangdong Police Training School. If there are not enough graduates to recruit, the county government will select and recruit outstanding police officers from the abolished public security bureaus and posts and assign them to work in the various district offices.

* If the location of the abolished public security bureau or post is a prosperous commercial area, the original income will be borne by the local people. If it is not the location of the district office but the location of a township office, the original income will be allocated to the township office. Township offices may also establish police officers as appropriate.

* The establishment of police officers in township offices should be handled in accordance with Articles 8 to 10 of these measures.

* District and township offices handling public security matters should comply with existing laws and regulations.

Suzhou: Kidnappers Tear Up Ransom Note; Open Coffin to Identify Body

A body was discovered in the river near Guanyin Mountain in the Suzhou countryside a few days ago. The upper body was wearing a short black coat, and the lower body was wearing blue pants. The hands and feet were tied, and a huge stone was tied to the waist. The prosecutor's office sent an investigator to conduct an examination and strictly investigate the murderer. The details have been [unclear] in the newspaper. It is now known that on the fifth day of the third month of the lunar calendar, Ding Zaoru, the son of Ding Gengquan from Dingjia Yan, Xutang Township, Chen Tomb, was kidnapped. Negotiations for the ransom took place but were unsuccessful. He has not been rescued to this day. The clothes and other items of the body found near Guanyin Mountain were identical to those of Ding Shenru. Ding Zigao, the brother of the deceased, petitioned the prosecutor's office to request identification of the body. The office dispatched police to accompany Ding Zigao to Guanyin Mountain on the 14th to open the coffin and identify the body. It was confirmed that it was Ding Shenru, who had been kidnapped and torn apart by the bandits, who had thrown his body into the river. The prosecutor's office was requested to strictly investigate the kidnappers to comfort the deceased.
