Taxpaying Chinese Association – Representative Assembly This Afternoon – Election of Chinese Directors and Executive Committee Members – Chairman Wang Xiaolai Returned to Shanghai Yesterday to Preside

Xin Sheng News Agency reports: The Shanghai Concession Taxpaying Chinese Association will hold its 15th First Representative Assembly at 2 PM this afternoon on the fifth floor of the Association’s premises at 59 Hong Kong Road, to elect Chinese directors to the Shanghai Municipal Council and executive committee members, and to discuss other important matters. Chinese directors and Chinese committee members of the Municipal Council will attend to report. The Association's Chairman, Wang Xiaolai, also returned to Shanghai last night to preside over today's meeting, and is scheduled to hold the first meeting of the Executive Committee at 3 PM on the 16th to elect a chairman and vice-chairman, three standing committee members, and to discuss the cases submitted by the first Representative Assembly of this session. The Chairman's speech and the Director's report are recorded below:

Chairman’s Speech

Speech by Wang Xiaolai, Chairman of the 15th First Representative Assembly of the Shanghai Concession Taxpaying Chinese Association: Representatives of the Shanghai Special City Party Department of the Chinese Nationalist Party, Representatives of the Shanghai Office of the Executive Yuan of the National Government's Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Representatives of the Shanghai Municipal Government, Ladies and Gentlemen, Today marks the establishment of the ninth Representative Assembly of the Taxpaying Chinese of the Public Concession, and it is also the day when this Representative Assembly holds its first meeting. In this autumn of internal troubles and external threats, which is even more pressing, the mission of this Representative Assembly, although entrusted only by the million residents of the First Special District of Shanghai, has a relationship, in form and in reality, that extends to the entire country, and even to the world. Therefore, the responsibility of this Representative Assembly is even more difficult than that of previous sessions. This is something that all representatives cannot deny or abandon. It is noted that the first meeting of the first Representative Assembly (April 1928) was chaired by Mr. Yu Qiaqing. His concluding remarks stated, "In short, if taxpaying Chinese wish to obtain real benefits, the legislative power is of utmost importance. However, if administrative and executive affairs are not presided over by Chinese, there will eventually be a situation where the tail wags the dog." Also, at the first meeting of the seventh Representative Assembly (April 1934), the chairman's speech legally recognized the status of this First Special District, characterizing the district's autonomous organs as "autonomous organs jointly managed by Chinese and foreign residents. If this can be evolved, and given a short period of transition, it is the most peaceful and straightforward method for unifying and completing the Shanghai Municipality." Although the impact of the above two points cannot be explained one by one, the enthusiastic participation of individual and group members of this Association is sufficient to indicate that their understanding of the future is real and accurate. The competition for rights should go hand-in-hand with the competition for obligations; otherwise, the competition becomes selfish. Our Chinese nation's love of peace, harmony, and propriety are indeed supreme virtues, but there should be limits, that is, to ask ourselves if our obligations are not inferior to others. Statutory rights should be strived for; otherwise, there will be problems in survival. Therefore, our people's enthusiasm for competing in the election of foreign taxpayers this time is considered unprecedented in the history of the Shanghai Municipal Council. However, we can regard it as an excellent lesson. What is regrettable is that after the ballots were counted, 323 unselected ballots were found in the empty ballot box, and they were added after the list of elected candidates was announced. This seems to be a misunderstanding. In 1931, during the major Yangtze River flood and the September 18th Incident, this Association sent a letter to the Municipal Council, in the form of a memorandum, requesting that they observe the economic situation and implement austerity policies. Although the Municipal Council did not deny it, it was not effectively implemented. During the first meeting of the previous Representative Assembly, the economic depression in this First Special District was almost indescribable. Therefore, the chairman's speech stated, "Judging from the current financial methods of the Municipal Council's income and the decline of the market, it will definitely be insufficient to meet expenditures next year." Fortunately, Mr. Ford, the Director of Finance of the Municipal Council, was adept at coping, and there were no major flaws. However, regarding the most important eight-year education plan that has been set to improve the educational level of citizens, it has not been implemented. After several consultations, only one Municipal Council primary school was established this year, and the education subsidy was increased by 19,000 yuan. This shows their straitened circumstances, which cannot be concealed. Judging from the Municipal Council's budget for 1936, although their act of cutting expenditures cannot be considered "preventing a fire before it starts," it is still commendable to "mend the fold after the sheep are lost." However, the "duplication of agencies" and organizations that provide entertainment for a very small number of people can still be seen in the budget, and it is difficult to understand what the intention is. In the speech by the chairman of the previous Representative Assembly, it was stated, "Individual expenditures must be based on income, but those who handle municipal affairs often despise the general economy of society, always expanding the budget year by year to show gradual prosperity, and some even consider it to be respectable." He also quoted the warning from former British Prime Minister MacDonald at the Lausanne Conference, "Public prosperity depends on individual prosperity," to urge the Municipal Council to pay attention to finance. At the same time, in order to help the Municipal Council open up new sources of revenue and reduce expenditures in finance, he proposed the implementation of cases such as collecting general vacant property taxes without violating the law. Unfortunately, the Municipal Council specializes in the method of "killing the goose to get the golden eggs," that is, not implementing the ratio of ten to one for property tax and land tax, but instead increasing the estimated amount of existing actual rent to increase the tax, and further invalidating the ratio of twenty to one stipulated in the Land Regulations. As a result, the total revenue from both property tax and land tax has actually decreased. This Representative Assembly should take this opportunity to urge the Municipal Council to pay attention. In terms of personnel, local talents should be selected as much as possible so that salary items can be saved. For equipment, construction, printing, and other materials, those with low prices and equivalent effects should be selected as much as possible to show people the fact of waste. Accumulating small amounts makes a large amount. The tax burden on taxpayers is lightened, and the Municipal Council's budget is also easy to balance. Why not do it? The population of this First Special District, with us as the masters, accounts for more than 95%, and the taxes paid, even based on the memorandum issued by the Municipal Council in 1927, not to mention that the actual number is more than this, is more than 55%. Therefore, the allocation of seats on the Municipal Council board, even if it does not follow the population ratio, should at least follow the tax ratio. Our Chinese directors on the Municipal Council should have at least ten seats. Regarding the issue of increasing the number of our Chinese directors on the Municipal Council board, there was a clear suggestion in the exchange of letters between this Association and the Municipal Council on March 26, 1928. Based on the words and spirit of the exchange of letters, this Association proposed increasing four seats on February 12, 1934. Unexpectedly, the authorities of the Municipal Council at that time forgot their own position and arbitrarily expressed their rejection beyond their authority. In their reply letter, they said, "Out of consideration for the public opinion of foreign residents, the foreign directors believe that increasing the number of Chinese directors is not yet the right time, and even if the proposal is put forward, it will not be supported by the representatives of the countries concerned." The chairman's speech at the previous Representative Assembly stated that these words have the following fallacies:

1. Dividing the entire Municipal Council into two parts, namely, the foreign directors and the Chinese directors. This is detrimental to the dignity of the Municipal Council.

2. Foreign directors unilaterally decide the rights of Chinese residents, completely stifling the opinions of Chinese directors.

3. Arbitrarily determining the opinions of the representatives of the countries concerned.

4. Still regarding A taxpayers as able to restrict or open up the rights of B taxpayers. Our people understand that increasing the number of Municipal Council directors means increasing responsibility. The manifestation of this responsibility is the taxpaying obligation. After having fulfilled obligations beyond rights for many years, putting forward this legitimate request is in line with the so-called "normal course of events" in the above-mentioned exchange of letters from the Municipal Council. This Representative Assembly should, based on legal principles and public opinion, express and implement genuine cooperation between Chinese and foreign residents, and resolve to "petition the government and authorize the Municipal Council to negotiate with the representatives of the countries concerned to increase the number of Chinese directors on the Municipal Council by four seats, starting from 1937, to show the sincerity of genuine cooperation." Those who understand the prosperity of this First Special District through cooperation should not hinder it, but should support it. The market in this First Special District is still in a slump. We should be of one mind and work together to make every effort to seek its revitalization. We also hope and urge the Municipal Council to follow the methods of the Shanghai Municipal Government in providing relief to the unemployed and safeguarding the poor, and to build public housing and run orphanages, etc., so that everyone can be properly cared for. Then the threat to security can be reduced day by day, and the defense funds used to suppress this threat can be transferred to "education" and "care." The work reports of the directors and committee members of this Association who attended the Municipal Council in the previous session can be found in the booklet. Please refer to it. We respectfully thank the Party and government representatives for their presence and supervision.

Director and Committee Report

Report on Participation in Government by the Directors and Committee Members of the Shanghai Public Concession Municipal Council for the Year 1935. We were entrusted by the previous Representative Assembly to serve as directors of the Municipal Council and committee members of various committees for the year 1935. One year has passed, and our term has expired. Today, we are pleased to attend the first meeting of the Representative Assembly for the year 1936. We respectfully report on the important matters related to our Chinese people that we have participated in during our term:

1. Allocation of Duties in the Administrative Committee: The powers and responsibilities of the various administrative committees of the Municipal Council, and their position in the administrative system of the Municipal Council, have been explained in detail in the previous report, and will not be repeated here. Although the number of committees has increased or decreased over the years, they have generally remained the same. There are currently twelve committees, not including those that are temporarily formed due to special circumstances. There are about 30 Chinese members, which is several times the number when Chinese first joined. Chinese people participate in all important matters. The Chinese School Subsidy Committee is composed entirely of Chinese people. The Library and Water Rate Review Committee are both chaired by Chinese people. The committee set up last year to review the telephone rate increase also hired Chinese experts. The Land Committee has increased two Chinese members, which is especially important for the amendment of the Yangjingbang Regulations. It has been formally approved by our government last year, and all legal procedures have been completed. According to the years of Chinese participation in government affairs, although the number of directors and committee members has increased, Chinese and foreign taxpayers are still not in an equal position, which is truly regrettable. Last year, we exchanged views with Chairman Arnold several times, and drafted methods as a basis for discussion. However, due to the importance of this matter, it is difficult to achieve success without careful and thorough consideration. We still hope that the representatives will uphold the inalienable rights of citizens and the equality of Chinese and foreign status, and urge the new directors and committee members to continue their efforts to achieve full success. We sincerely hope so. The list of our committee members on each major committee is as follows: Finance Committee: 8 seats, 3 Chinese seats, held by Xu Xinliu, Wang Yansong, and Xi Yushu; Police Committee: 9 seats, 3 Chinese seats, held by Yu Qiaqing, Jiang Yiping, and Xi Yushu; General Affairs Committee: 8 seats, 3 Chinese seats, held by Guo Shun, Wang Yansong, and Zhu Wenqi; Staff Committee: 8 seats, 3 Chinese seats, held by Yuan Ludeng, Guo Shun, and Xi Yushu; Public Utilities Committee: 8 seats, 3 Chinese seats, held by Feng Bingnan, Jiang Yiping, and Yu Hualong; Health Committee: 9 seats, 3 Chinese seats, held by Chen Jicheng, Yu Hualong, and Xu Xiaochu; Transportation Committee: 12 seats, 4 Chinese seats, held by Yu Qiaqing, Jiang Yiping, Xi Yushu, and Zhu Wenqi; Education Committee: 9 seats, 4 Chinese seats, held by Lin Kanghou, Liu Zhanen, Ou Yuanhuai, and Xi Yushu; Library Committee: 5 seats, 2 Chinese seats, held by Xu Xinliu and Chen Jicheng.

2. Retention or Abolition of the Music Band: The proposal to improve the music band in order to reduce municipal spending has been made for a long time. Last year, the proposal to abolish the band or transfer it to a private institution was simultaneously submitted to the Chinese and Western taxpayers' meetings, and the results were either yes or no, and no consensus was reached. The Bureau then formed a music subcommittee to consider this issue in detail. The subcommittee recommended that the existing music band be disbanded and a new band be formed, based on the principle of economic efficiency. The annual cost should not exceed 200,000 yuan. The members of the new band should sign separate employment contracts and should not enjoy the benefits enjoyed by other Municipal Council employees. The organization is tentatively set to have a director, a deputy director, and a brass band instructor, each with one person, and 44 members. After repeated assessments by the board of directors, they did not want to make a decision immediately, and planned to seek the opinions of taxpayers before proceeding with the review. If taxpayers believe that the music band should still be retained, then the reorganization should be approved according to the subcommittee's recommendations, in order to save costs. If the annual expenditure does not exceed 200,000 yuan, then the savings should be 80,000 yuan, which would be a small supplement to the municipal treasury. The concert will still be held as usual this year. Students from the National Central Conservatory of Music will participate in the performance from time to time, which is a rare event and has won great praise.

3. Improvement of the Transportation System: This city is densely populated and vehicles block the roads. In recent years, the Bureau has repeatedly improved the transportation system. The previous report described it in detail. When the Chief of the Police Department was on leave, he was instructed to consult extensively at any time to see whether it would be more beneficial to hire an expert to handle transportation matters, or to use existing personnel to specialize in it. The Chief of Police Department then appointed a Deputy Inspector on leave to go to the traffic department of the Scottish police district to practice managing pedestrians and vehicles, in order to adopt it and observe its effectiveness. Other important matters related to transportation include:

(1) Improving the Transportation Regulations and Restricting Parking: Any vehicle parked in a busy city is only allowed to park within a limited time and must not be delayed arbitrarily. On the roads between Xiaoshadu Road and the Bund, parking is not allowed for more than half an hour from 8 AM to 6 PM, and violators will be punished. This new regulation was decided in April last year and will be implemented after a nine-month postponement, followed by a two-month notice.

(2) Issuing Licenses to Drive Small Rental Cars: This was approved by the Transportation Committee, but when the Board of Directors reviewed it, they thought that the service of small cars might not be as good as that of larger models, and that their structure was not strong enough, which could easily lead to accidents. They also felt that they would make traffic more crowded, so they rejected it.

(3) Amending New Regulations to Ban Random Honking: No car shall have more than two horns, and any horn that makes a loud noise shall be prohibited. Only sharp, short sounds are allowed. In addition, except for special circumstances, no vehicle is allowed to use the horn when it is stopped. This new regulation came into effect on October 3. At first, many drivers were punished for violating the regulations, but as the ban gradually became known, everyone complied. The noisy sounds in the city on a daily basis, which disturbed people's minds, were reduced a lot, and it has been effective.

4. The General Situation of Chinese-Foreign Relations: Chinese and foreigners live together in the concession, and they share prosperity. Therefore, all municipal facilities must be based on harmonizing ethnic sentiments and promoting local prosperity. In recent years, there have been debatable aspects of Chinese-foreign cooperation, but there are also some that can be permitted. In the summer of 1934, the National Government promulgated regulations prohibiting the private storage and smuggling of goods. Last year, the Bureau and the Customs authorities agreed on methods to assist in searching shops in the concession for contraband. If such a case occurs, the Legal Department will file a public prosecution with the First Special District Court for legal punishment. In addition, various agencies in our country have sent trainees to the Bureau for internships. This year, many people from Nanjing and Hangzhou were sent to various administrative offices for training, with special emphasis on firefighting, finger-printing research, and firearms identification. The responsible personnel gave separate guidance and detailed explanations, which were highly valued by various authorities in our country. In addition, Chinese-foreign county-related cases, such as cross-border road construction and factory inspections, have not been resolved due to the complexity of the relationship, which is an obstacle to cooperation and should be addressed as soon as possible in order to eliminate them.

(Handling of the Telephone Issue: Last year, the Shanghai Telephone Company applied for a price increase because its operating income was insufficient to pay interest. When citizens heard about this, they strongly opposed it. The Chinese and Western Taxpayers' Annual Meetings simultaneously passed resolutions authorizing the Municipal Council to form a special committee to explore the entire case. The Bureau followed the wishes of the taxpayers and proceeded to organize the special committee. Initially, it was planned to have four committee members, one each from China, Britain, Japan, and the United States, and to hire one telephone expert to assist. Later, Japan requested that a Japanese expert be added, but our country believed that this case was closely related to the interests of the Chinese people. Without the participation of Chinese experts in the research, the interests of the Chinese people would inevitably be ignored. Therefore, the Board of Directors decided to change the committee to an expert committee, composed of one expert each from China, Japan, Britain, and the United States. The Chinese expert was borrowed from Mr. Hu Ruixiang, Director of the Nine Provinces Long-Distance Telephone Engineering Office of the Ministry of Communications. The number of charges was scheduled to be implemented in January this year, and it was recognized that there was still an urgent need to reduce the company's operating expenses. In November, the experts' report was submitted to the Board of Directors for review. We proposed that the implementation period be postponed by two months. If the company's operating income exceeds the amount of interest, the price should be reduced immediately, and various expenses should be reduced in accordance with the experts' recommendations to reduce the burden on users. After discussion, it was agreed that the current price would be used as a trial period for one year. All surplus reserves, which should be half owned by the company, were cancelled with its consent, also for a period of one year. The length of each call should not be restricted. Various installation fees should be reduced according to the prices set by the experts. As for the company's calculation of profits and losses, such as the payment of income tax to the US government and the management fees of the International Telegraph and Telephone Company, there is room for negotiation. The income tax item is not within the scope of the contract and should not be borne by users. The management fees paid to the international company (calculated at 4.5% of the total income per year, about 300,000 yuan) should not be borne by Shanghai for a long time. As for depreciation, the Bureau borrowed money at the end of the year before last to help the company change its debt from gold to silver. Therefore, the amount of investment should be reduced by 3 million yuan, and the amount of annual depreciation can also be greatly reduced. These three items should be further discussed and properly handled by the Bureau and the company, in order to maintain the interests of users and to live up to the deep trust of taxpayers.

(Investigation of Household Registration in the Concession: The investigation of household registration in the concession is scheduled to be held once every five years. Last October, it was held as usual. The calculation is based on the total number of people who spent the night in the survey area on the night of October 23. The survey forms are explained in Chinese, English, Japanese, and Russian. The Bureau also asked the Municipal Government and the French Concession Board of Directors to work together to ensure the accurate number of households in Shanghai, the age of each household, and the population density in each district. The Bureau investigates the foreign household registration in the cross-border road construction area, and the Municipal Government provides the number of Chinese households. The Chinese aspect of this survey is more advanced than the previous one in four aspects:

1. In the past, Chinese household registration was only divided into adults and children. This time, it is divided by age.

2. In the past, servants were listed separately for each household. This time, they are included in the occupation item.

3. A separate item is listed to indicate how many homes there are in each household.

4. A detailed breakdown of the number of people in each occupation of Chinese citizens is provided. The results of the survey have been published. There are 51 nationalities. The number of Chinese citizens is 1,120,860 (excluding the cross-border road construction area). The number of foreign citizens is 38,915. The total number of Chinese and foreigners is 1,159,775. If calculated as a percentage, Chinese citizens account for more than 96%, and foreign citizens account for less than 4%. The difference in numbers is so great. Compared with the previous survey, the number of Chinese citizens has increased by 149,463, and the number of foreign citizens has only increased by 1,618.

(Current Situation of Drug Prohibition in the Concession: Since the National Government adopted a six-year plan to strictly ban opium, the drug situation in the concession has been of concern to us. Last year, the Bureau drafted a drug prohibition report and submitted it to the League of Nations. According to the investigation by the Police Department, drug use is still a serious problem in this city. It is deeply hidden and difficult to eradicate. Although it seems that there has been a decrease in the number of opium smokers, the number of users of morphine and heroin is increasing day by day, and there is a rapid rise to replace opium. Therefore, the amount of raw and cooked opium seized is decreasing day by day, while the amount of heroin seized is increasing sharply. The registration of opium addicts is still being carried out slowly in the concession, and the exact number is unknown. In the year before last, 7,996 opium offenders were arrested, and 6,655 were convicted, which is a considerable number. The Bureau is making every effort to crack down on the manufacture and sale of drugs at any time. The difficulty is that there are often large-scale international drug traffickers who forge names, fraudulently obtain passports, and sneak into Shanghai to buy and sell drugs for sale to other countries. The number of manufacturers of morphine and heroin is also increasing day by day. Therefore, it is difficult to cope with. Crude morphine is often smuggled from the Sichuan-Yunnan area to Shanghai, which is also one of the reasons for the sharp increase in the number of private drug manufacturers.

(Progress of Chinese Education: The educational policy of the Municipal Council has been divided into two major outlines since the Education Committee redefined it in 1931:

1. Establishing Municipal Schools

2. Subsidizing Private Schools

In recent years, educational administration has been carried out in accordance with these two outlines. Last year, the Japanese Residents' Association suggested stopping the establishment of new schools and transferring all construction funds to subsidies. The Bureau's Education Committee expressed its opinion that this move is contrary to the current education policy. The current policy is to build new schools and subsidize private schools, and the two should be carried out in parallel and complement each other. It is not advisable to be biased. It is not advisable to concentrate educational construction funds on subsidizing private schools, which would be a great waste of effort. This was approved by the Board of Directors, and the original educational policy was maintained. As for the educational facilities for Chinese people last year, in terms of building new schools, the Education Committee initially recommended continuing the eight-year school construction plan, adding one primary school and one girls' middle school. However, the Board of Directors felt that the local economy was declining, tax revenues were short, and the municipal treasury was exhausted, so they decided to first build one primary school, accommodating more than 500 people, using the existing school buildings of the Xinvxue on Penglu Hanbili Road. Another night school will be established in the eastern district, specializing in the reception of female workers, teaching simple knowledge. Both schools have opened one after another. There are now four Municipal Chinese schools, with 2,341 students, one girls' middle school, with 840 students, six primary schools, with 4,000 students, and one night school, with 800 students. Except for Chinese middle schools, all schools are headed by Chinese principals and teachers. Chinese middle schools have also been approved by the Ministry of Education, and students can participate in the joint examination. Those who pass can be admitted to national universities. The curriculum has also been revised and implemented in accordance with the standards set by the Ministry for many years. Each school now has a Chinese vice-principal, and the Bureau plans to find ways to transfer Western teachers and gradually reduce them. As for subsidizing private schools, it has been expanded year by year since it was implemented in 1932. The initial subsidy was 110,000 yuan, which has been increasing year by year. It is now nearly 130,000 yuan. There are 36 middle schools and 187 primary schools that receive subsidies, with a total of 46,111 students. The Bureau has formed a private school subsidy committee to be responsible for the distribution of funds. The Health Department sends staff to inspect each school from time to time, and those whose sanitary facilities do not meet the regulations can be suspended from payment. As for teaching, its quality is still supervised and guided by the Education Bureau of the Municipal Government, to show that the educational power belongs to it and cannot be transferred. Some of the above points may be known to you, and some may not be known to you, but what is important is that they are the important policies implemented in the concession in the past year, which can be asserted. We are not good enough, but we were entrusted by the previous Representative Assembly to take on the difficult task of dealing with Chinese-foreign relations and being responsible for local administration. We are often short of talent and ability. It is difficult to live up to the ardent expectations and strict supervision of the citizens, and we feel guilty. However, our love for the country is the same as that of the wise, and our desire to protect our rights has never been behind others. We have made every effort to protect the welfare of the people and the sovereignty of the country, and we have done our best. This is enough to reassure you. As for other administrative affairs in the concession, the annual report for 1935 is sent to each taxpayer by this Association every week and will be completed soon. It discusses them in more detail. It will be sent to the secretariat of this Association within days and can be read at any time. What is not covered in this report is detailed in it. Directors Yu Qiaqing, Xu Xinliu, Guo Shun, Jiang Yiping, and Xi Yushu; Committee Members Wang Yansong, Lin Kanghou, Yu Hualong, Chen Jicheng, Zhu Wenqi, and Xu Xiaochu.

Verdict on Bribery Case of Patrol Officer

Ge Yunpeng, a patrol officer of the Second Sub-bureau of the Public Security Bureau of Houqiao Town, arrested gamblers at the home of a villager, Pu Fucheng. Pu Fucheng bribed him with ten yuan, which was split and used by police officers Wang Qinglin, Qi Mingxuan, Chen Xiang, Yang Yaochao, and Chen Jinrong. After police officer Chen Ziming reported this to Patrol Inspector Chen Shaohua, Ge Yunpeng and others were transferred to the court for trial. Yesterday was the scheduled date for sentencing. Judge Liu presided over the court, sentencing Ge Yunpeng to three years and six months in prison, and Qi Mingxuan to six months, suspended for three years. After the sentencing, they were taken back into custody. Wang Qinglin and the other four were released on bail and therefore were not sentenced.

Completion of Road Paving on Changzhou-Lishui Road

After the opening of the Su (Jiangsu) - Li (Shui) Road (from Wujin to Lishui), traffic was initially allowed on the earthen road, and business was quite good. However, since the road surface had not yet been paved, vehicles had to stop during rainy weather, causing considerable inconvenience to travelers. The authorities dispatched special personnel and allocated funds to implement the paving of the road surface in sections, which has now been gradually completed. From now on, the road should be unobstructed, allowing cars to run on schedule. Shen Zhe from the Jiangsu Provincial Highway Administration Department departed from the province today to inspect the road construction along the route and provide instructions.

Planning to Establish a Women's Reformatory

Xu Baoguang, the Director of the Wuyi Public Security Bureau, believes that punishing and releasing prostitutes who are arrested does not fundamentally solve the problem, as they gradually return to their old habits. He has specifically suggested to the county government that a women's reformatory be established, so that prostitutes can be housed and educated to fundamentally eliminate prostitution. The county government raised this issue for discussion at the tenth day political affairs meeting, deciding that the Public Security Bureau and the Relief Institute should jointly consult and formulate concrete measures, and then submit them for review and establishment.

On Financial Policies During Extraordinary Times

— Xiao Shuyu

Today, Dr. Yin Chu gave a speech at the Nanjing Zhongshan Society on "Financial Policies During Extraordinary Times." According to his analysis, the main sources of revenue for our country are customs duties, salt taxes, and consolidated taxes. When extraordinary times arrive, these taxes will become unreliable. First, because the seaports will be blockaded, foreign trade will come to a standstill, so there will naturally be no customs duties. Second, because the main salt fields are located in the southeastern coastal areas, they will inevitably be occupied. Once the salt fields are lost, there will be no salt tax to collect. The consolidated tax relies on Shanghai, Tianjin, and other major commercial ports. At that time, these places will be destroyed or occupied, so the consolidated tax will also be unreliable. Since the above tax revenues have no hope, and at the same time, public bonds cannot be issued because there is no collateral, lacking funds, the only thing left is to inflate the currency. However, issuing too much currency will make restoration difficult in the future. Finally, he proposed two methods as countermeasures:

Implement the collection of income tax,

Limit the inflation of currency.

The above is a summary of Dr. Ma’s speech. (Mr. Jian Shishi has a record of his speech.) I find his analysis and conclusions very valuable for research, but I cannot completely agree with them. Therefore, at that time, I simply expressed my different opinions. Here, I also quote his records for research.

Regarding Dr. Ma's analysis, I believe it is indeed worth considering, but it is inevitably too negative and pessimistic. Let us try to estimate it from both the revenue and expenditure aspects of the country.

From the revenue side, the total budget for the 24th year is 957,154,006 yuan, of which 341,361,400 yuan is from customs duties (accounting for more than 35%), 184,219,044 yuan from salt tax (accounting for more than 19%), and 113,298,177 yuan from consolidated tax (accounting for slightly less than 12%). These three items account for the absolute majority of the country's net income. If Dr. Ma's predictions come true, the country's finances will be in dire straits. But the reality is not that simple. Even in terms of customs duties, although the enemy may be able to blockade our southeastern coast, they may not cut off traffic to Guangzhou and Hong Kong. If not, our foreign trade during extraordinary times will not be completely nonexistent. As for salt taxes, although the main coastal salt fields may be occupied, we can stockpile large quantities in advance. Moreover, the land and well salt from Sichuan can also supply the consumption of several provinces. If our country's preparations are well managed, and salt is publicly sold, the revenue should not be less than the current salt tax. Finally, when it comes to the consolidated tax, it is even more complex and flexible. If the government and the people are unprepared in advance, and the so-called southwestern and northwestern construction plans are just empty words, then naturally there will be no consolidated tax to collect. Otherwise, if the government can lead and assist the people in implementing the "economic policies for extraordinary times" briefly listed below, then the domestic nascent industries will prosper because the seaports are blockaded and fewer foreign goods flow in. In this way, the consolidated tax will not necessarily be without hope. According to my analysis above, our country's main tax revenues during extraordinary times will only be partially reduced, and will not be as severe as Dr. Ma described.

It is not enough to determine financial policy solely from the amount of revenue. Therefore, we also need to analyze and study the expenditure side. According to the general budget statement for the 24th year, the expenditure is 957,154,006 yuan. Although the highest amount is for military expenses (328,000,000 yuan), we assume that this expenditure will increase during extraordinary times. However, the expenditure next to military expenses is debt service, totaling 175,803,279 yuan, of which 145,222,190 yuan is for domestic debt principal and interest, 44,556,057 yuan for foreign debt principal and interest, 33,908,706 yuan for the Boxer Indemnity, and 40,442,852 yuan for loans. This expenditure can of course be completely suspended during extraordinary times. The next largest expenditure is subsidies (101,980,089 yuan) and financial expenses (66,011,343 yuan), education and cultural expenses (37,211,621 yuan). The expenditure on finance and education can of course be reduced at that time. The main item in most of the subsidies is the total amount to be planned by each province under the national defense construction item in the future. In addition, although the expenses for national affairs and party affairs are not very large, they can also be reduced by more than half. As for the expenditure figures at that time, no one can assume them at this moment, it depends on the requirements of the environment and reality. But it is undoubtedly necessary to expand the budget more than usual.

After briefly discussing our country's current general budget, I will move on to the main topic. Dr. Ma regards the collection of income tax as the main countermeasure in financial policy during extraordinary times. I am very skeptical of this proposition. Of course, I am sympathetic to the implementation of income tax collection, but according to the Ministry of Finance's estimates, the annual income is only more than five million (listed as five million in the general budget). But excluding the more than four million yuan currently collected from public servants for income tax donations, there is only slightly more than one million benefit. Moreover, once extraordinary times arrive, public servants can only receive the minimum maintenance expenses, so where will there be income tax to collect? Other employees such as teachers, doctors, lawyers, factory workers, shopkeepers, and bankers will inevitably have their income reduced due to the impact of current affairs, and income tax will naturally be reduced. Therefore, using income tax to enrich the country's finances during extraordinary times is akin to drawing a cake to satisfy hunger. (To be continued)

Local News

Jiangnan Shipyard's Largest Dock Opens Yesterday

Ms. Ma Mingqu cuts the ribbon; the Ninghai warship enters the dock for the first time.

The No. 3 dock built by the Jiangnan Shipyard of the Navy was completed at the end of last month. The opening ceremony was held yesterday afternoon at 3:30 p.m. Chen Jiliang, Vice Minister of the Navy, presided over the ceremony, and Ms. Ma Mingye, daughter of Ma Deji, Director of the Jiangnan Shipyard, cut the ribbon. The ceremony was solemn and enthusiastic. The ceremony was held at 3:30 p.m., and attendees included Chen Jiliang, Vice Minister of the Navy, Ma Deji, Director of the Jiangnan Shipyard, Lin Yuanquan, Director of the Ordnance Department of the Navy, Huang Xianqi, Staff Officer, Wu Zhennan, Director of the Coastal Defense Office, Fang Ying, Director of the Pilot Training Institute, Liu Depu, Director of the Survey Bureau, Cai Baoqi, Battalion Commander of the Navy Guard Battalion, Cao Yijing, Director of the Aircraft Manufacturing Department, Chen Pengfan, Director of the General Affairs Department of the Jiangnan Shipyard, and section chiefs Yu Jianfu, Liang Xunying, Ye Zaifu, Guo Xizhi, Yan Shouhua, Captain of the Yongji warship, Gao Yishen, Captain of the Ninghai warship, engineer Sheng Qunhe, soldiers from various warships, students from the Jiangnan Shipyard's workers' children's school, and about a thousand guests.

A glimpse of the venue: The dock is the largest in the country and can accommodate 20,000-ton ships. It was designed by the American World Industries Corporation and constructed by the Xinheng Construction Company. The engineer was Sheng Qunhe. The ceremonial platform was set up in the north of the dock, with a portrait of Sun Yat-sen hanging in the center, and the Party and national flags hanging above it. The surroundings of the venue were decorated with various colored ship flags. The entrance to the dock was covered with colorful ribbons. The Navy Guard Battalion was stationed along the way to maintain order. The Ninghai warship was designated by the Navy to perform the dock entry ceremony.

Ceremony Held: After the ceremony was performed according to protocol, Chen Jiliang, Vice Minister of the Navy and Commander of the First Fleet, reported on the construction process of the dock. Then music was played, and the Ninghai warship slowly entered the new dock amidst the melodious music. Ms. Ma Mingqu, holding鲜花, accompanied by Captain Gao Xianchen, stood in front of the ship. When the Ninghai warship approached the ribbon, Ms. Ma waved the scissors and cut the ribbon. A burst of firecrackers erupted, and the ceremony was completed. Then, the staff of the shipyard entertained the guests, showed them around the various departments of the factory, and served tea and snacks until about 4 o'clock.

Construction Process: The Jiangnan Shipyard originally had two docks, one over 500 feet long and the other over 400 feet long. It has historically undertaken a large amount of construction and repair of medium-sized warships and merchant ships of around 10,000 tons. From the 21st to the 24th year of the Republic, Chen Shaokuan, Minister of the Navy, concurrently served as the director of the shipyard. Considering that there were no large-scale facilities in the country's shipyards, and that there was often insufficient supply during the annual dock inspection of naval vessels and various merchant ships, which was detrimental to the maintenance of the shipping industry, he began to build the third dock in May of the 22nd year. The first phase was completed by October 10th of the following year. Its scale was already one of the largest in our country. Chen continued to promote and expand it, ordering Ma Deji, the director of the shipyard, to continue to work hard, and painstakingly raising funds to support it amidst difficult financial circumstances. His determination to construct it was unparalleled. Therefore, on April 1st of the 24th year, construction was started again, extending the dock by several hundred feet. Today, it has been completely completed, with a total length of over 640 feet, a width of 100 feet, and a depth of 20 feet. Both sides are built with steel sheet piles and filled with cement. The gate is rectangular, and the pumping room is built next to it. The solidity of the engineering and the novelty of the layout can be called great. From now on, when large ships from various countries come to Shanghai, they can enter the dock with ease and conduct inspections, which will greatly benefit the future of the shipping industry.

Opening ceremony of the large dock at Jiangnan Shipyard (Photo by Lin)

Ding Shaoji Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday

Will Go to Nanjing to Report Today or Tomorrow

Ding Shaoji, a counselor at the Chinese Embassy in Japan, was transferred back to China. He arrived in Shanghai yesterday afternoon at 3:00 p.m. from Japan aboard the Japanese ship Shanghai Maru, accompanied by his son and others. Zhou Jue, Director of the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Deputy Director Zhao Tiezhang, and Zhang Mengling, among others, all welcomed him at the Huishan Wharf. After disembarking, Ding rested at the New Asia Hotel. He is scheduled to go to Nanjing tonight or tomorrow morning to pay respects to Foreign Minister Zhang and Interior Minister Jiang and report. According to Ding, who spoke to a Central News Agency reporter on board, he was transferred back to China because he had private matters to attend to in Shanghai, so he planned to stay in Shanghai for a day or two before going to Nanjing to report, and because he had been away from his hometown for a long time, he would take the opportunity to return to his ancestral home in Hubei before going to Nanjing to take up the position of expert member of the Treaty Committee of the Ministry. As for Sino-Japanese diplomatic issues, he has now left his position and is not in a position to express any opinions. According to what he personally knows, after the political changes in Japan, there will be no changes in Japan's foreign policy toward China or toward Europe and the United States. Although the situation between Japan and Russia is frequently tense, it is unlikely to lead to war, because although Japan is urgently preparing for war domestically, it does not advocate war. The candidates for ambassador to China include Shigemitsu Kawa and others, but no decision has been made yet. Ding continued to say that Japan's industry and commerce have developed greatly in recent years, and the social economy has naturally been affected by the global economic downturn, but the impact on overseas Chinese in Japan is still slight.

Mr. Ding Shaoji (left) arrives in Shanghai (Photo by Lin)

Conflict with Police Detectives Yesterday; Many Trams and Buses Damaged; Shops Temporarily Closed; Both Sides Injured; Mediation by Chinese Directors Expected to Prevent Escalation

Dagon News Agency reports that the Public Concession's Labour Committee of the Municipal Council previously restricted the number of rickshaw pullers registered and reduced rickshaw fares, which was opposed by the rickshaw owners, leading to a strike on the first of this month. After mutual consultation, a solution was reached to reduce rickshaw fares, but the registration of rickshaw pullers would continue, scheduled to begin yesterday, but only allowing 5,000 people. The rickshaw owners stated that there should be no restrictions on registration. Yesterday morning, as many as 20,000 rickshaw pullers went to register, demanding that the registration office increase the quota. Due to the large number of people and the complexity of the situation, disturbances occurred. The police went to suppress them, resulting in minor injuries to several people. This matter has been mediated by the Chinese directors of the Municipal Council, and the situation may not escalate.

Quota of 5,000, 20,000 Arrive: The Labour Committee of the Municipal Council scheduled the registration of rickshaw pullers to take place at the sampan factory in the west of Shanghai, at Ma Gen Road, east of the new bridge, on the 14th of this month, but only allowed 5,000 people. The rickshaw owners believed that there were no fewer than 60,000 to 70,000 rickshaws in Shanghai, and even if 40,000 people registered, there would still be many who did not register. If there were such restrictions, they would be unemployed, so they immediately expressed their opposition, demanding that unrestricted registration continue. Yesterday, the Municipal Council held the registration at the rickshaw puller registration office in Shun De Lane on Ma Gen Road. According to the registration procedures, the rickshaw puller should first obtain an application form from the registration office with the owner's road permit for the fourth month, and then the rickshaw puller should be recommended and registered at the registration office. The recommendation method is that each rickshaw or every two rickshaws recommend one person, and three rickshaws recommend two people. There are 10,000 rickshaws in Shanghai, so 5,000 rickshaw pullers can be recommended. However, when registering yesterday morning, more than 20,000 people went directly to the registration office on Ma Gen Road to demand registration, resulting in considerable disorder.

Many People and Noise Cause Disturbances: The registration office of the Labour Committee was originally scheduled to start registration at 8:00 a.m., but given the large number of rickshaw pullers who arrived and the chaotic order, it was impossible to start. At that time, a few rickshaw pullers were still loudly calling for an increase in registration. Because there were too many rickshaw pullers, the area from the eastern end of Ma Gen Road registration office to the sampan factory on Carter Road was the concentration area of rickshaw pullers, and traffic was almost blocked. At this time, several hooligans from outside suddenly loudly demanded an increase in registration, and a small number of rickshaw pullers echoed them, and then disturbances occurred.

Vehicles Damaged and Traffic Cut Off: At this time, the Public Concession's No. 10 bus passed through the area of Carter Road and Ma Gen Road, and the No. 19 trolleybus also passed through Carter Road and Ma Gen Road. They were stopped and attacked. The bodies were hit with small stones, causing much damage to the glass windows, totaling nine vehicles. However, the passengers in the car were not injured. However, pedestrians on the road were frightened and fled. Later buses and trolleybuses and other vehicles were afraid of being involved, so they dared not go. The Public Concession immediately dispatched a large number of police officers from the New Zha and Gordon Road police stations to prevent the situation from escalating and to prevent bad people from mixing in. They temporarily ordered the vehicles to cut off traffic. At the intersection of the Chinese concession at the New Sampan factory and the new bridge, only people from the concession were allowed to cross the bridge to Zhabei, and people from Zhabei were not allowed to cross the bridge to the concession. The police station agreed with the Public Security Bureau's New Zha Branch and the city's security team to send police officers and security teams to guard the bridge to maintain order. The disturbances among the rickshaw pullers occurred at 9 o'clock.

Police Suppression, Minor Injuries on Both Sides: At ten minutes, the police immediately sent Chinese and foreign police detectives to suppress them. At that time, there was a slight disturbance, because there was a conflict between the rickshaw pullers and the police, resulting in about ten rickshaw pullers being injured by wooden sticks and sent to the hospital. (According to the police, only one person was injured by being pushed down, and one person was detained by the police.) On the Western police side, Officer No. 1853 had his right eye injured and his pistol was also knocked off. He has now been sent to Baolong Hospital for treatment. Because the injury is not serious, there is no major problem. There was also Western detective Crowe and Western Deputy Head Moffatt who were slightly injured, and Chinese Deputy Head Tao Shiwei was also injured by stones.

Shops Closed and Registration Temporarily Suspended: After such disturbances lasted for half an hour, they stopped. The Municipal Council dispatched a large number of police officers, distributed from Carter Road and New Zha Road to the northern end of the Sampan Factory, the new bridge, and the area of Gordon Road and Ma Gen Road, to prevent accidents, and closed the iron gate of the new bridge, leaving only a one-meter wide sidewalk for pedestrians to enter and exit. The Western District Branch of the Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Association on Ma Gen Road sent a large number of detectives to guard against accidents. When the incident occurred, the shops along the way closed their doors to prevent beatings. They began to open their doors and do business as usual after 10:00 a.m. Traffic, such as buses and trolleybuses, etc., also resumed after 10:00 a.m., and everything returned to normal, but the police detectives were still stationed there. After this incident occurred, the registration office of the Labour Committee of the Municipal Council announced the temporary suspension of registration.

Detailed Statistics of Injuries to People and Damage to Vehicles: Regarding this sudden incident, according to investigations by the Dagong News Agency reporters to various parties, it was learned that more than ten rickshaw pullers were slightly injured, one police detective was injured, one Western police officer was injured, and a pistol was lost. As for the No. 10 buses that were damaged, there were four in total, with registration numbers 15063, 15033, 15026, and 15009. There were five trolleybuses damaged, with numbers 32, 322, 356, 299, and 302. All of them had damages to the glass and bodywork, but there were no major problems. The loss of the above nine buses and trolleybuses is around several hundred yuan.

Statement by the Labour Committee on This Matter: The person in charge of the Labour Committee issued the following statement to the Dagong News Agency reporter yesterday afternoon after the incident: This morning, more than 10,000 people went to the rickshaw puller registration office on Ma Gen Road to make trouble, but these more than 10,000 people were not rickshaw pullers, but mostly unemployed hooligans, and a very small number of rickshaw pullers who were exploited, as well as garbage collectors. Because according to the rickshaw puller registration method, the rickshaw owner must first obtain an application form, the rickshaw pullers were unwilling to make any expressions on that day. The reason why the Labour Committee restricts the registration of rickshaw pullers to only 5,000 people is none other than to seek to remedy the exploitation of rickshaw pullers and protect their interests. As for the reasons for the restrictions, the Labour Committee has previously published them. The Labour Committee will still accept rickshaw pullers who register with a letter from a rickshaw owner in accordance with formal procedures. According to the Labour Committee's investigation, most of the rickshaw pullers in Shanghai have already been registered, and there are really fewer than 20,000 who have not yet registered.

Rickshaw Owners' Expression on This Matter: The Dagong News Agency reporter also consulted with the persons in charge of the rickshaw owners last night about their views on this matter. According to them, today's matter is purely a problem of rickshaw pullers demanding a livelihood and has nothing to do with the rickshaw owners. However, the rickshaw owners had previously notified the Municipal Council that there are still 20,000 to 30,000 rickshaw pullers who have not yet registered. If the Municipal Council only restricts the registration of 5,000 people, there will inevitably be too many monks and too little gruel, and it will not be enough to distribute. Today, unfortunately, disturbances occurred. The rickshaw owners only hope that this matter can be resolved as soon as possible. Before the Labour Committee of the Municipal Council has a clear solution to this matter, the rickshaw owners do not want to make any expressions for the time being.

Chinese Directors Took Office Last Night to Mediate: The Chinese directors of the Municipal Council, Yu Qiaqing, Xu Xinliu, Jiang Yiping, etc., consider this matter to be a serious problem in the Public Concession, and they cannot bear to sit idly by and allow this matter to be delayed. They specifically contacted the Labour Committee and the rickshaw owners last night to mediate the rickshaw puller disturbance case yesterday morning, in order to resolve it as soon as possible, and asked the rickshaw owners to persuade the rickshaw pullers not to take any further action. The rickshaw owners have agreed and are willing to do their best to explain to the rickshaw pullers. At the same time, the representatives of the Rickshaw Owners Association, Yin Zhiling and Hou Shaoan, visited the chairman of the Labour Committee, Macy, and members Zhu Maocheng and Wang Zhiren at the Municipal Council yesterday morning to discuss the handling methods.

Whereabouts of Contemporary Figures

Soviet Russian Ambassador to China, Bogomolov, accompanied by his wife and secretary, arrived in Shanghai by train from Nanjing yesterday morning and went to the official residence to rest. Ju Zheng inspected the judiciary in Zhejiang and took a car to Shanghai at 8:30 yesterday morning.

Zhang Zhijiang and Tan Zhen took the night express train to Nanjing last night.

Guizhou Missionary Bosshardt Out of Danger; China Inland Mission Has Received Telegram

The Shanghai office of the China Inland Mission received a telegram on Tuesday stating that Guizhou missionary Bosshardt was out of danger. He is now safely residing in northwestern Yunnan Province. His two family members, who were abducted by bandits and communists, escaped on the second day of the abduction when the bandits were chased by government troops. Mr. Hayman was released by the bandits in November last year. Only Mr. Bosshardt was trapped in the bandits' lair for eighteen months, enduring hardship. He has now been released. It is reported that no ransom was paid.

Fish Market Board of Directors Hold Meeting: Banquet for Wang Xiaolai and Others

Wang Ding to Enter Beijing Tonight to Consult Wu on All Matters; Board of Directors to Discuss and Amend Business Regulations This Morning

The Shanghai Fish Market, sponsored by the Ministry of Industry, held its inaugural meeting in Shanghai on the 10th. After the election of officials and business representatives to the board of directors and supervisors, preparations for its establishment were actively underway. Mr. Wang Xiaolai, the General Manager of the market, returned to Shanghai yesterday. The Standing Committee of the Board of Directors held a banquet last night at the East Asia Restaurant to welcome Standing Director Wang Xiaolai, Deputy Managers Zhu Kaiguan and Sun Yichen, and former Manager Yu Kaizhan. Among those present were Standing Director and Chairman of the Board of Directors Du Yuesheng, Standing Directors Tang Chengzong, Fang Jiaobo, and Gui Yanfang. Standing Director Xu Tinghu was unable to attend due to a trip to Beijing. The meeting discussed the market's preparation policy, the date of takeover, and other matters, adjourning at 9 p.m. Mr. Wang Xiaolai is scheduled to take the night express to Beijing tonight to consult with Minister of Industry Wu Dingchang on all matters. He is expected to return to Shanghai tomorrow and plans to take over the fish market on the 17th, appointing Directors Lin Kanghou and Zhang Fayao as the receivers. The Ministry will send Secretary Qian to supervise the inventory. The Board of Directors is also scheduled to hold a standing meeting at 10 a.m. today. The market preparatory committee specially notified Directors Du, Tang, Fang, Xu, Gui, and Wang of the meeting, scheduled for 10 a.m. on the 15th of this month, at the Zhonghui Building, 1st floor, to discuss business regulations. It is also understood that today's meeting will only discuss business regulations, so only Tang Chengzong, Qu Hemen, Fang Jiaobo, Gui Yanfang, and Yu Kaizhan will attend. These five individuals have been designated as responsible for amending the regulations. General Manager Wang Xiaolai and Deputy Managers Sun Guchen and Zhu Kaiguan will also be present. According to Tang Chengzong, Standing Director of the Shanghai Fish Market, the establishment of the market is primarily to assist the fishing industry, to promote the production and sales of fish through regulation, and to reduce the burden on fishermen. Following the Japanese fish market's fish cargo sales procedure, producers (i.e., fishermen or fish farmers) sell their fish to wholesalers, who then seek to sell it to the fish market. The market uses an auction method, with brokers buying and then reselling to fishmongers, who then sell directly to consumers. Thus, fish passes through five stages from production to consumption. The current transaction sequence in Shanghai's fish industry is: producers sell to fish shops, fish shops sell to fishmongers, and fishmongers sell to consumers, only four stages. Historically, the focus of fish trading in this city has been on the fish shops, a practice that has been followed for many years. Fish shops and producers have various deep business relationships. Once the market opens, if the centuries-old habits are suddenly changed, there will inevitably be many obstacles. In the future, a gradual approach will be adopted to achieve the purpose of establishing the fish market. As for the fishermen, they are eager for the establishment of the market. Representatives of offshore fishermen, such as Xu Yifei, have been campaigning and appealing, as repeatedly reported in the newspapers. The reduction of the burden on fishermen after the opening will be strived for. In short, the business regulations of the fish market are currently being revised, taking into account the above situation and considering all aspects. They will be submitted to the Board of Directors for approval and then submitted to the Ministry of Industry for promulgation. As for the takeover date, it has been decided to proceed on the 17th of this month.

Anti-Smoking and Anti-Drug Propaganda Week: First Preparatory Meeting Held Yesterday; Organizational Regulations and Implementation Proposals Approved; Propaganda to Begin on the 20th

——Lantern Parade on the 26th Evening——

The Municipal Party Headquarters, in conjunction with various sectors, is holding an Anti-Smoking and Anti-Drug Propaganda Week. Yesterday (the 14th) at 2 p.m., it convened the first preparatory meeting, gathering representatives from relevant agencies and organizations to discuss the implementation plan. The meeting proceedings are recorded as follows:

Representatives Present: Guo Lanqing from the Songhu Garrison Headquarters, Zhang Shengcai and Duan Dingfeng from the Chinese National Anti-Drug Association, Wang Shaoqi from the Shanghai Municipal Government, Dai Lizhen from the Municipal Public Security Bureau, Yuan Hongjun from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Cai Bubai from the Municipal Anti-Smoking Committee, Yu Yaoqiu from the Municipal General Labor Union, Lu Jingshi and Huang Xianggu from the Municipal Party Headquarters, etc. Chairman: Lu Jingshi; Recorder: Du Mengsen. The meeting commenced as scheduled.

Chairman's Report: The Chairman began by stating that the meaning of anti-drug efforts is well understood by everyone and need not be elaborated upon. The Central Government and the National Government are determined to ban smoking and drugs, so various regions are actively carrying out anti-drug work. This city is currently registering. In order to make citizens aware of the harm of opium and drugs, this committee, in accordance with the Central Government's intentions, has organized a preparatory committee for the Anti-Smoking and Anti-Drug Propaganda Week. He hoped that various agencies and legal entities would cooperate in carrying out the work. The discussion then began.

Resolutions: Passed the organizational regulations of the Shanghai Anti-Smoking and Anti-Drug Propaganda Week Preparatory Committee (Resolution: Amended and passed). Passed the implementation plan of the Shanghai Anti-Smoking and Anti-Drug Propaganda Week Preparatory Committee (Resolution: Passed). Election of Standing Secretaries and Secretaries of Various Sections (Resolution: (A) The Municipal Party Headquarters, Municipal Government, and Garrison Headquarters were elected as Standing Secretaries. (B) The Municipal Party Headquarters was elected as Documentation Secretary. (C) The Municipal Government was elected as Finance Secretary. (D) The Garrison Headquarters, Public Security Bureau, and Shanghai Municipal Anti-Smoking Committee were elected as Design Secretaries. (E) The Shanghai Municipal Anti-Smoking Committee, National Anti-Drug Association, Municipal Education Association, Public Security Bureau, Municipal Farmers' Association, General Labor Union, Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and Municipal Boy Scout Council were elected as Propaganda Secretaries). Decision on Preparatory Expenses (Resolution: Provisional budget of 800 national currency units, with the Municipal Government contributing 300 units, and the Garrison Headquarters, Public Security Bureau, Shanghai Municipal Anti-Smoking Committee, Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and Municipal Party Headquarters each contributing 100 units). Setting of Office Hours (Resolution: Office hours set from 9 a.m. to 4 p.m. daily. The Municipal Party Headquarters, Municipal Government, Garrison Headquarters, Public Security Bureau, and Shanghai Municipal Anti-Smoking Committee will each send a representative to be stationed in the office daily). The meeting adjourned at 4 p.m.

Organizational Regulations: "Organizational Regulations of the Shanghai Anti-Smoking and Anti-Drug Propaganda Week Preparatory Committee" (Article 1) The name of this committee is the Shanghai Anti-Smoking and Anti-Drug Propaganda Week Preparatory Committee. (Article 2) This committee, in accordance with the Central Government's intentions, aims to expand anti-smoking and anti-drug propaganda in this city. (Article 3) This committee is composed of eleven agencies and legal entities, including the Municipal Party Headquarters, Municipal Government, Public Security Bureau, Garrison Headquarters, Municipal Farmers' Association, General Labor Union, Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Municipal Education Association, Shanghai Municipal Anti-Smoking Committee, National Anti-Drug Association, and Municipal Boy Scout Council. (Article 4) This committee has eleven secretaries, who are appointed by the initiating agencies and legal entities. (Article 5) The secretaries elect three standing secretaries from among themselves to manage daily affairs. (Article 6) The standing secretaries have four sections: documentation, finance, design, and propaganda. (Article 7) The scope of work of each section of this committee is as follows: "Documentation" handles the committee's documentation affairs under the guidance of the standing secretaries; "Finance" manages the committee's revenue and expenditure; "Design" handles the design of various propaganda materials; "Propaganda" is responsible for all matters related to propaganda. (Article 8) The detailed rules for each section's work are to be determined by each section itself and implemented after approval by the standing secretaries. (Article 9) The committee's work plan will be formulated separately. (Article 10) The preparatory expenses are as follows: 100 yuan for bamboo cloth banners, 100 yuan for cloth propaganda pictures, 200 yuan for 10,000 propaganda booklets, 200 yuan for colorful slogans, 100 yuan for lantern expenses, and 100 yuan for other expenses. The above expenses will be shared by the Municipal Government, Public Security Bureau, Garrison Headquarters, Shanghai Municipal Anti-Smoking Committee, Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and Municipal Party Headquarters. (Article 11) The committee's address is temporarily located at the Municipal Party Headquarters. (Article 13) Any matters not covered in these regulations shall be submitted by the secretaries to the secretaries' meeting for amendment. (Article 14) These regulations shall be implemented upon approval by the secretaries' meeting.

Implementation Plan: "Implementation Plan of the Shanghai Anti-Smoking and Anti-Drug Propaganda Week Preparatory Committee" This plan is formulated in accordance with Article 9 of the organizational regulations of this committee. This plan takes the promotion of anti-smoking and anti-drug efforts as its scope of work. This committee designates April 20th to April 26th as the city's Anti-Smoking and Anti-Drug Propaganda Week. The schedule is as follows: Day 1 (April 20th): All Sectors Propaganda Day, Expanded Commemoration Week in the morning. Day 2 (April 21st): Party Headquarters Propaganda Day, (A) The Municipal Party Headquarters instructs subordinate party branches to organize propaganda teams to go out and promote. (B) The Municipal Party Headquarters sends personnel to broadcast speeches. Day 3 (April 23rd): Academic Circles Propaganda Day, (A) The Municipal Education Association guides students from various schools to organize propaganda teams to go out and promote. (B) Invite celebrities to broadcast speeches. Day 4 (April 23rd): Entertainers' Broadcasting Propaganda Day, This committee formulates propaganda outlines and sends them to the Entertainment Association to instruct all members to promote during broadcasting. Day 5 (April 24th): Film Propaganda Day, (A) Screen anti-drug films. (B) Movie theaters show anti-smoking and anti-drug propaganda slides. Day 6 (April 25th): Various Organizations Propaganda Day, The Municipal Farmers' Association, General Labor Union, Municipal Chamber of Commerce, National Anti-Drug Association, and Municipal Boy Scout Council separately hold propaganda activities and instruct them to organize propaganda teams to go out and promote. Day 7 (April 26th): Lantern Propaganda Day, The preparatory committee, in its name, sends letters to various agencies, organizations, schools, and party branches in the city to participate. Detailed measures will be formulated separately. Commentaries on anti-smoking and anti-drug efforts are to be published in newspapers and magazines, and more articles and illustrations on the propaganda should be written and drawn during the propaganda week. A letter should be sent to the Municipal Education Bureau instructing the deans of student affairs of various schools in the city to include this anti-smoking and anti-drug propaganda as one of the students' holiday assignments. The method should be centered on each student's family, and then spread widely and deeply into the community, so that they deeply understand the government's determination to ban smoking and drugs, and take the relevant plans and laws as a propaganda test. The specifications for various propaganda supplies are as follows: (A) Bamboo cloth banners to be hung on main transportation routes. (B) Bamboo cloth pictures to be hung on main transportation routes. (C) Propaganda booklets to be distributed at gatherings and lantern parades. (D) Colorful slogans (E) Lantern slides (F) Others. When gathering for lantern parades, lanterns, candles, and other items are to be provided by the participants themselves. Any matters not covered in this plan are to be amended by the secretaries' meeting at any time. This plan is to be implemented upon approval by the preparatory committee's secretaries.

National Goods Groups Hold Banquet for Wu Dingchang: Promoting National Goods Does Not Mean Excluding Foreign Goods

The China National Goods Production and Sales Cooperation Association and the China Industrial Foreign Trade Association held a banquet at the Bank Association Club at 12 p.m. the day before yesterday to welcome Wu Dingchang, Minister of Industry, and factory inspection specialists Cen Depeng and Gu Yuchuan. The guests included Minister Wu, Cen Depeng, Gu Yuchuan, Wang Shiding, Liu Shimu, Pan Yangyao, and others, as well as factory representatives Cai Shengbai, Chen Diexian, Fang Yexian, Wang Xingyao, Hu Xiyuan, Xiang Kangyuan, Zhang Huikang, Lao Jingxiu, Fang Jiange, Ren Shigang, Ye Youcai, Xu Xiaochu, Hu Shicheng, and others, totaling more than 60 people. During the banquet, Chairman Zhang Huikang delivered a welcome speech, stating that it was an honor for the national goods community that Minister Wu could come to provide guidance amidst his busy schedule. Minister Wu was also a leader in the industrial and commercial community, so he knows the pain of the industrial and commercial community and will certainly be able to improve and expand our industry and commerce in the future. Minister Wu then delivered a training speech, saying that national goods factories have made significant progress in their difficult operations. The government feels that the current economic situation is closely related to politics and pays great attention to development. Therefore, the Executive Yuan has sent specialists to inspect various national goods factories. On the government's side, it is currently trying to promote the sales of national goods. At least in the three items of clothing, food, and housing, we must use our own goods. Soviet Russia is also an economically backward country, but they wear less, eat less, live less well, and use the best things to exchange for the tools produced by other countries. We can certainly wear well, eat well, and live well, but we cannot use our own Chinese goods, because our own things can provide us with comfortable production in terms of clothing, food, and housing. Our promotion of national goods does not mean excluding foreign goods. We should still make the most of foreign goods for production tools. As for the manufacture and promotion of national goods, that still depends on the efforts of the factories themselves. The government will, of course, help as much as possible within its power. In addition, Cai Shengbai, Wang Xingyao, Lu Zhixue, Xiang Kangyuan, and others successively expressed their opinions on improving industry and commerce. The guests and hosts dispersed happily at around 3 p.m.

Beijin Steamer Runs Aground at Shihuzui: Currently Offloading Cargo and Passengers

The Beijin steamer of the Zhidong Shipping Company at 122 Guangdong Road, which sails to ports such as Shanghai, Tianjin, and Niuzhuang, has a gross tonnage of 2,500 tons, a load capacity of 1,663 tons, a net registered tonnage of 1,031 tons, a ship length of 253 feet 2 inches, a width of 37 feet 4 inches, a depth of 19 feet 6 inches, and a public horsepower of 136, with a speed of 10 nautical miles per hour. The ship was built in 1903 and was originally named Dorathor Riokmer. It was purchased by Zhidong. On the 10th of this month, it sailed south from Tianjin fully loaded with goods.

Encountering Fog and Running Aground

On the morning of the 11th, the ship arrived at the Longkou sea area outside Zhifu, near Shihuzui. There was fog on the sea, and the ship ran aground on a hidden reef. The hull was stuck and could not move. The shipowner initially wanted to use full speed to reverse and get off the shoal, but because there were many goods and passengers on board and the draft was deep, the shipowner did not dare to move the ship again. He urgently telegraphed for help from Yantai, Tianjin, Longkou, and other places. The Shanghai branch also received this report yesterday.

Offloading Cargo and Passengers

Currently, several barges have been dispatched from Yantai and Longkou to the Shihuzui area. First, the passengers will be transferred to Longkou, and then the cargo in the hold will be completely unloaded and stored in the Longkou warehouse. Then, the bottom of the hold will be inspected for any holes. Only then can the ship be lightened with the high tide and floated to the surface. It can then be towed out of the shoal. The extent of the loss is currently unknown.

Bank of China and Hunan Construction Department Agree on Rural Loan Methods: Total Amount of 500,000 Yuan; Two Districts Designated for Loan Disbursement

In order to assist farmers, increase agricultural production, and reduce agricultural costs, the Bank of China has agreed with Yu Jichuan, Director of the Hunan Construction Department, on rural loan methods. Wang Benren was dispatched from the Rural Loan Department of the Shanghai Head Office to Changsha to investigate and designate Qiyang and Hengyang in Southern Hunan and Feng County in Western Hunan as loan areas. The total loan amount is tentatively set at 500,000 yuan. If effective, it will be expanded. The loan methods consist of fourteen articles, stipulating mortgage and repayment methods, which are quite thorough.

Foreign Tea Firms Association: Representatives Returning to Shanghai After Petitioning in Anhui; General Meeting of Members Convened the Afternoon Before Yesterday to Report; Principle of Official Transportation and Commercial Sales Adopted

The Shanghai Foreign Tea Firms Association, opposing Anhui Province's control of tea leaves, dispatched representatives Sun Zifu, Zhuo Huapu, Zhuo Jingcheng, and others to Anhui to petition the Directors of the Finance and Construction Departments, requesting the abolition of the tea transport and sales association that controls tea leaves in order to maintain the merchants' hardship. Directors Liu and Yang met with them separately and agreed to handle the matter flexibly and to have a tea sales office organized by tea merchants to manage it. The three returned to Shanghai from the hospital the day before yesterday and held a general meeting of members at the association's office on Beijing Road at 3 p.m. to report on the petition process. Then, they began to discuss the flexible measures newly set by the Anhui Provincial Government, that is, the principle of official transportation and commercial sales, which was adopted. It was also decided to report to the Anhui Construction and Finance Departments that the association would handle the matter accordingly. The meeting adjourned at around 4 p.m. The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, which had previously requested that the government be telegraphed to abolish the tea transport and sales association established by the Anhui Provincial Government to control tea leaves, received a reply from the National Economic Council yesterday, saying, "To the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, we have received the Qing telegram. This matter is mainly handled by the province. We have forwarded it to the Anhui Construction Department to take into account the tea firms' operations in order to alleviate merchants' hardships. Sincerely, the National Economic Council."
