Boiling Oil Accidentally Splashed on Young Girl's Face, Causing Excruciating Pain and Rolling on the Ground, Cold Water Poured Over Her

The day before yesterday evening, a Ningbo woman, Dai Zhou, residing at No. 17 Xuexi Street in the city, took her six-year-old daughter, Xiangjun, to Wenfuqi Noodle Restaurant at No. 3 Xueqian Street for refreshments. After they sat down, the restaurant staff, eager to cook noodles for the arriving customers, moved the oil pot used for stir-frying on the stove, replacing it with a noodle pot. Unexpectedly, due to carelessness, the boiling oil in the pot splashed onto the girl's head, face, hands, and feet. Instantly, she experienced excruciating pain and rolled on the ground. At that moment, the terrified restaurant staff poured a basin of cold water over her, causing the skin on her head and face to completely peel off, and blood gurgled out. Her mother, who was nearby, was also burned on her arm. The patrol police officer on duty at the scene rushed to the scene and quickly sent the injured to the Southeast Hospital for treatment. The restaurant staff, Chen Yunfa and Ren Fangshu, as well as Xiangjun's mother, Dai Zhou, were taken to the police station for questioning.

Zheng Meikang Sues Mother-in-Law for Enticement Due to Wife's Departure, Wife Arrives in Court During Trial, Acquittal After Investigation

Zheng Meikang (26 years old), a postal administration employee from Ningbo, residing at No. 221, Changle Lane, Dixiwei Road, married Yang Shimei (21 years old), a woman from the same hometown, in 1931. Since the marriage, Yang attended China Women's Middle School. Recently, she became pregnant and gave birth this month. Due to a difficult labor, she was sent to a sanatorium for delivery. She gave birth to a boy. When she returned home on the 31st of last month, Yang left with the child around 7:00 PM on April 1st without saying goodbye. That night, Yang's mother, Yang Guo, went to Zheng's house to demand the return of the person. Zheng Meikang believed that his mother-in-law had come to his house a few hours before his wife left, so he suspected that his mother-in-law, Yang Guo, had enticed his wife to hide. He filed a lawsuit against his mother-in-law with the First Special District Court for the crime of disrupting the family. Since his wife took away a 1,000-yuan deposit book from Siming Bank when she left, he filed a civil suit demanding its return. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Xiao Xie [blank] of Criminal Court No. 5 summoned him for questioning. Zheng Meikang stated the previous situation in his petition and requested legal punishment. Yang Guo stated that on April 1st, because her daughter returned home from the hospital, she prepared some dishes and went to visit her. She returned home soon after. She did not know about her daughter's departure beforehand and had no enticement. She only found out after being notified by the plaintiff's family. Yang Shimei was also summoned to the case by Judge Xiao. She stated that after she gave birth in the hospital, the plaintiff was unwilling to pay the medical expenses and only paid them after being forced to, but he was reluctant. After returning home, her aunt and the other woman expelled her, saying that if she didn't leave, they would beat her. She had no choice but to leave with the child and live at her maternal uncle Guo Jinhe's house in Pudong. It was not her mother's instigation. Subsequently, witnesses Dai Hu, Xu Wang, Li Chunquan, Shen Boliang, etc. were presented by both parties. Some proved that Yang Guo did go to Zheng's house before Yang Shimei left, and some proved that Yang Shimei did go to her maternal uncle's house that night. Judge Xiao reviewed the testimony and acquitted Yang Guo in court and dismissed the plaintiff's incidental civil suit. He also instructed both parties to reconcile out of court and not to litigate, so that the feelings of both parties would not reach an irreparable point.

Inland Waterway Shipping Association Strives to Eliminate Cargo Boat Tax, Subcommittee Has Drafted Report, Requests City Chamber of Commerce to Submit to Central Relief

According to Guowen News Agency, the local Inland Waterway Shipping Industry Association believes that the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau's collection of cargo boat tax on tugboats is illegal and duplicates taxation, so they have unanimously protested and organized a subcommittee to study and discuss the protest methods and their legal basis. A subcommittee has drafted a report on the results of the discussion and submitted it to the 71st Executive Committee of the association for approval. The following is a summary of the conclusions of the report: Before the promulgation of the Regulations on the Management of Tugboats, the Finance Bureau's collection of cargo boat tax does not violate the law. Although the boat tax is a legitimate local tax, tugboats pay boat money to the customs on a regular basis, so the Finance Bureau's additional collection of cargo boat tax is indeed a duplication of national income. The nature of Shanghai's civil boats is different from tugboats, so they cannot be exempted from boat tax by analogy. Therefore, the city's boat tax will not be affected by the elimination of cargo boat tax on tugboats. Tugboats are vessels that pay tax to the customs and should be treated the same as steamers, port sailboats, etc. They meet the legal basis of Article [blank] of the Shanghai [blank] Special City Regulations for Eliminating Cargo Boat Penalties. The Detailed Rules for the Collection of Boat Tax by the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau were only amended and promulgated by the Municipal Government's instructions on February 11, 20th year of the Republic, and were not submitted to the Ministry of Finance for review and record in accordance with the Interim Law on Supervising Local Finance, which is a dereliction of duty to collect from the people. After the association passed the report of the subcommittee, it decided to continue to strive to achieve the goal of eliminating the tax. Its letter (letter from the president omitted) and attached report requested the City Chamber of Commerce to submit it to the Central Political Council [blank] the Executive Yuan to continue its efforts.

The various publications printed by the association are also distributed to all sectors of society for free and have never been charged. Recently, a certain Western newspaper in Shanghai published information about the New Life Movement publications in Guan under the name of the association, which not only damages the reputation of the association, but also hinders the promotion of the New Life Movement. In order to avoid misunderstandings from all parties, in addition to sending a letter to the public security organs for investigation, it is solemnly stated again that if such situations are found in the future, it is hoped that they will be sent to the local public security organs for investigation in accordance with the law, so as to serve as a warning to others. After receiving the report, the local New Life Movement Promotion Association has transferred a letter to the Municipal Public Security Bureau, ordering it to pay attention to the investigation.

China Foreign Joint Relief Association Relief General Association Transfers Four-Province Cooperation Undertaking to Economic Committee for Handling

The China Foreign Joint Relief Disaster Relief General Association, located at No. 505 Henan Road, is the pioneer of rural cooperative societies in China. There are now more than 1,000 societies in Hebei Province, and there are plans to gradually promote them in various provinces. In the spring of 1932, the association was entrusted by the National Government's Flood Relief Committee to handle the closure of agricultural relief in the four provinces of Anhui, Jiangxi, Hunan, and Hubei. After the closure, the association's offices in Anhui and Jiangxi and the Hunan and Hubei sub-associations separately organized rural cooperation matters in their respective provinces, which achieved considerable success. Farmers found it convenient. Later, the National Economic Committee was established, and all the undertakings of the Flood Relief Committee were transferred to its jurisdiction. In November 1934, the Righteous Relief General Association believed that the four-province cooperation undertaking was entrusted in nature, and since a competent authority had been established, it should be transferred to it for handling. It sent a letter to the Economic Committee requesting it to take it back and handle it itself, but it has not been implemented yet. [blank] After the Economic Committee established the Cooperative Undertaking Committee, it sent a letter to the Consultative Relief General Association in December last year, requesting them to separately inform the Anhui and Jiangxi offices and the Hunan and Hubei sub-associations to compile a roster of employees, as well as a list of society names, files, funds, and public property, and send them to the committee first, so that they could arrange to send personnel to take over. The Righteous Relief General Association followed the instructions and sent special commissioners Xiong Guoqing and technician Wang Wu Ke to take over separately. All the procedures were completed last month, and the directors of the Cooperative Committee's offices in Anhui, Jiangxi, Hunan, and Hubei were stationed there, and their work was proceeding as usual. The rest of the personnel remained unchanged.

Xu Fuji, Judge of the Second Branch of the High Court, Is Accused of Debt Incurred by His Late Father, Xu [blank] Pursues More Than 11,000 Yuan, Transferred to Second Special Court Due to Jurisdictional Error

Xu Fuji, the current judge of the Civil Court of the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, is the son of the late lawyer Xu Bingcheng. When his father was practicing law in Shanghai, he had [blank] grievances with Xu [blank], who resided in Xiangxing Lane on Aierjin Road. Lawyer Guo Ci-mei Sues Zhu Yun-wang for Defamation

Alleging Improper Conduct with His Daughter-in-law

Lawyer Guo Ci-mei, 39 years old and a native of Minhou, Fujian, joined the Shanghai Lawyers' Association as a member in May of the 4th year of the Republic [1915], practicing law. Recently, he suddenly filed a private prosecution with the Criminal Court of the District Court, accusing Zhu Yun-wang, a local merchant residing at No. 12, Tianzhutang Street, South City, of fabricating facts and defaming him, etc. The complaint stated in brief: In the autumn of last year, the plaintiff was engaged by the defendant's daughter-in-law, Zhu Shen Jing-fen (i.e., Mrs. Zhu Shen), who came to the plaintiff's office to request that the plaintiff represent her in a lawsuit before your court, seeking support from the defendant. The litigation lasted for a year and has already been finalized after three trials. Zhu Shen, burdened with heavy debts, requested to temporarily store her dowry and spare parts, etc., with the plaintiff, so that she could go to other ports to raise funds. The plaintiff, feeling pity for the orphaned woman, agreed to the storage. Unexpectedly, the defendant seized upon this as a pretext to falsely accuse the plaintiff of improper conduct with Zhu Shen. Subsequently, during the three trials, he fabricated facts in the complaint against Zhu Shen in various ways, damaging the plaintiff's reputation. All the newspapers in this city have reported on this. According to his actions, it is clear that he intended to defame the plaintiff. Therefore, the plaintiff requests legal action. Based on the complaint, the court, at 3:30 PM yesterday afternoon, had Criminal Court Presiding Judge Cai Ding-cheng preside over the trial in Criminal Court No. 12. The plaintiff, Guo Ci-mei, appeared in court and stated the prior circumstances. The defendant, Zhu Yun-wang, did not appear due to illness, but sent a lawyer as his agent, who replied that he had not yet received a copy of the plaintiff's complaint, did not know the cause of the case, and was unable to respond. He requested a postponement, which the presiding judge granted, and then the court adjourned.

Li A-lin Saved After Jumping into the Huangpu River

Around 4:30 PM the day before yesterday, on the Zhapu Road Bridge over the Suzhou Creek, a young man suddenly jumped into the river to commit suicide. Fortunately, a Chinese constable, number ten, from the Customs Water Police Station, saw him and quickly rescued him. He was brought back to the police station, where he identified himself as Li A-lin, 29 years old, from Tongzhou. He stated that due to unemployment and boredom, he had recently come to Shanghai from his hometown, seeking his brother but failing to find him. He then went to the Zhou residence to look for a friend, also without success. Mr. Zhou, taking pity on him, gave him ten silver dollars, intending to start a small business to make a living. However, while walking along Rue du Consulat in the French Concession, all the silver dollars vanished. In extreme frustration, he became weary of the world. The head constable instructed the officers to send him to the Tongxiang Association for assistance.

This reserve includes 7,351 taels and 5.5 mace of standard gold, valued at 50,779, equivalent to 373,324.70 Customs Gold Units. Letter to the Editor

To the esteemed editor of Shen Bao: Upon reading the "Local News and Miscellany" column of your newspaper on the 12th of this month, the news item "The Tiān Hòu Gōng Temple in Hongkou to be Consecrated Tomorrow" contains inaccurate facts, which has caused misunderstandings in the outside world and numerous inquiries. Upon investigation, our school has been established for more than ten years, and all the former site of the Tiān Hòu Gōng Temple and all the buildings have long been renovated and used by the school. The former shrines and other objects have also been burned. Therefore, the location of the Tiān Hòu Gōng Temple in Hongkou mentioned in your newspaper is not at our school and has nothing to do with the school. We hereby send this letter for clarification and request that you check and correct the facts. Sincerely, Zhai Shu-rong, Principal of Shanghai Municipal Shuji Primary School, April 14, 25th year of the Republic [1936].

Shanghai Municipal Council Health Report

The Straw Hat Industry in Shanghai, compiled by China Credit Information (Shanghai Industry and Commerce Overview, No. 22)

Overview: The straw hat industry in Shanghai is divided into two categories: straw hat export firms and straw hat factories. Their business nature is completely different. The former uses imported materials, hand-woven by workers, and sells them abroad. The latter uses domestic straw braids, manufactured by machines, and sells them domestically. The two organizations are different and do not communicate with each other, but their speed of development and severity of decline are the same. The export of straw hats has been around for twenty years. At first, foreign firms in China used the low labor costs in our country to distribute golden silk grass and Manila hemp from Luzon to farmers in Ningbo, Yuyao, and Haimen to weave, and then sold them to various countries. Later, Chinese merchants established their own export firms and traded directly with foreign merchants. The foreign firms found it difficult to compete, so they gave up one after another. The 19th year of the Republic [1930] was the golden age of straw hat export firms. Later, due to the decline in purchasing power of various countries, coupled with the impact of Japanese paper hats and Italian rough hats, the market plummeted. The issue of raw material supply was also rumored that the Philippine government would ban exports, causing considerable panic. Looking back, the straw hat factory in Shanghai has only been in existence for over ten years, from its inception to its decline. In the 19th year of the Republic [1930], there were no less than ninety straw hat factories in the city, and those that announced their closure one after another were numerous. The rise of small-scale straw hat factories in the interior in recent years is also an important factor in the decline of Shanghai's straw hat factories.

Raw Materials and Manufacturing of Straw Hats: The raw materials for straw hats are divided into golden silk grass, Manila hemp, glass grass, and straw braids. Golden silk grass and Manila hemp are produced in Luzon, glass grass is produced in Switzerland, and straw braids are produced in the mountains of Hebei Province, etc. Those produced in Yexian, Yangxin, Cangxian, and Nanle are the most famous. In terms of value, glass grass is the most expensive. Roughly, the cost of each straw hat is 1.3 yuan for glass grass, 8 jiao for golden silk grass, and 8 fen for Manila hemp. Straw braids are made of wheat straw, and the quality varies. High-quality braids are worth 150 yuan per package, and rough braids are worth 40 yuan. Each package contains 240 pieces, each piece 120 yards long. Each package can make 50 dozen straw hats. Straw braid firms in Shanghai include Hengfeng, Hongxiangyuan, Qianhe Yong, and Hongchangxiang. In the 23rd year of the Republic [1934], imported Japanese wax-lined braids entered the market. Manufacturers were tempted by the profits. After the Fuyuan Straw Hat Factory tried it, many followed suit for a time. This type of braid is a semi-finished product and must be waxed and woven before it can be used. Currently, there are three wax-lining factories in Shanghai: Huacheng, Hefeng, and Gongli. Wax-lining braiding factories include Tianlun and Hongchang. Japanese wax-lined braids are a kind of cotton fabric that becomes soft when exposed to moisture, unlike our straw braids, which are durable. If users can distinguish them, they will know the flaws of Japanese goods.

Straw hat manufacturing is divided into manual and machine-made. Manual weaving is a superior product, which is exported. Machine-made hats are mostly rough and determined goods, which are used by all classes. Women in Ningbo, Yuyao, Haimen, and other places in our country, regardless of age, regard weaving straw hats as a sideline. In its heyday, it reached fifty residents. The procedure is simple, easy to learn, and the tools used are just a block of three-dimensional round wood. Export firms set up zhuang-kou in the above-mentioned areas, distribute raw materials, and entrust them to weave. After they are made, they are paid according to the quality of the work. Those who are skilled in weaving can produce one hat every five days. On average, they can also weave two or three hats per month. In the 19th year of the Republic [1930], the average monthly wage per person was 20 or 30 yuan. However, this piece-rate method often had drawbacks, such as mixing rough goods with fine goods, or reducing the ingredients. Therefore, current merchants sell raw materials and then buy them from farmers. After straw hats depreciated, export firms reduced wages for farmers in order to reduce costs. The female workers who used to earn an average of 30 yuan now earn only 10 yuan. These hat-weaving women must have artistic ideas, because foreign straw hat styles change suddenly, sometimes high-crowned, sometimes flat-crowned. Export firms pay attention to them at any time. When there are changes, they use leaflets or sound gongs to inform them, and they are happy to accept them. Ningbo and Yuyao mostly weave golden silk and glass hats, while Haimen mostly weaves Manila hemp hats. This is probably just a matter of habit.

The manufacturing period of straw hat factories in Shanghai is usually from January to June. After this period, large factories weave woolen hats, and small factories weave casual hats. The machines used to make straw hats are generally straw hat machines from the Singer Company. The Shanghai factories with the most equipment have 22 straw hat machines, and the least have one. There are 500 units in the city. The manufacturing steps are: 1. Winding the straw braid into the predetermined style of the straw hat. 2. Organize the semi-finished straw hat. 3. Add glue and Ding or cowhide glue. 4. First rough drying. 5. Pressure machine. 6. Install cloth and leather rings. 7. Second drying.

Types of Straw Hats: The types of straw hats vary due to different raw materials. Strictly speaking, there are no less than 230 types. Generally, they are divided into three types: golden silk hats, Manila hemp hats, and glass hats. Golden silk hats can be divided into special, super, first-class, second-class, third-class, fourth-class, fifth-class rough goods. Manila hemp hats and glass hats also have super, first-class, second-class, third-class, fourth-class, fifth-class, and substandard goods, but only lack a special grade. The straw hats woven by Shanghai straw hat factories have always been divided into soft hats and hard hats. Since the import of Japanese wax-lined braids, there have been cotton wool products and mixed products of cotton wool and straw braids, but they are generally called straw hats.

Straw Hat Business: The straw hat export season is from September to April of the following year. Foreign additions in summer are only a coincidence. Australian business is mostly based on orders during the fall season. Export firms have agents in New York, London, Paris, and Hamburg. The firms report the prices of goods to foreign firms at any time and negotiate by telegram. If a transaction is concluded, the firm will issue a sales order, recording the color, quantity, price, and delivery date. It is stipulated that foreign bank customers must open a bank letter of credit by telegram. Some firms also credit foreign customers, remit their own remittances, or sell off. The Straw Hat Export Association has formulated business regulations to protect the interests of the industry. Among them, Article 10, which belongs to foreign firms, states: 1. Those who fail to open a bank letter of credit or delay in doing so, 2. Those who unreasonably return goods, 3. Those who abuse the price of goods, 4. Those who have gone bankrupt or have no credit may notify the industry and stop dealing with the foreign firms. (To be continued)

Spring and Autumn

Random Notes

— (Tang Zeng-geng)

A person's genius, whether mediocre or outstanding, cannot determine his future failure or success. A mediocre genius, if he can work hard and bury himself in hard work without fear of any difficulties, will eventually achieve satisfactory success. On the contrary, a person with outstanding genius who relies solely on his own genius and is arrogant and careless, will end up falling deeply into the trap of failure. Therefore, I advise all my mediocre genius friends, please do not lose the courage to work hard because your genius is mediocre, and do not be content to be backward and passive; at the same time, those friends with outstanding genius, please do not ruin your bright future because of your outstanding talent, and of course, you cannot despise everything because of your luck.

A life gained by genius is bitter and uninteresting. A life gained by struggle is meaningful and worthy of praise. Friends, there are two paths of "genius" and "struggle" in front of you. Which one will you choose?

Miscellaneous Words from Piaocheng

— A Yuan

Jiangbei Yancheng is also known as Piaocheng because of its shape. It is a first-class county in Lixiahe, so there is a commissioner stationed in the political aspect: in the economic aspect, the three banks of China Communications Farmers have branches; in the transportation aspect, Xiaolun is connected to Funing in the north, Dongtai in the east, and Taizhou Xinghua Shaobo in the southwest. In recent years, there have been Fuhu offshore vessels passing through the Nanyang port of the county, making it easier to transport salt and cotton. The newly planned Haidong Railway is also planned to be extended to this place; the prosperity of the future can be expected.

Education in Yancheng is extremely developed, and there are many people who are promoted to schools, with a total of about 1,000 university graduates, which is one of the best in Jiangsu. However, most of them study liberal arts and law, and if they have nothing to do at home, they run small newspapers, so there is a trend of advocating litigation. Recently, Shi Kuiling, a specialist, launched a campaign to stop litigation, but I am afraid it will not help. The general people are simple, hardworking, and good at saving. Although their daily life is simple clothing and vegetarian food, they are not affected by occasional famines. Compared with people in the Suzhou and Shanghai area, who wear silk clothes but have no rice for dinner at home, they cannot be compared.

In Lixiahe counties, such as Taizhou, Dongtai, Xinghua, and Yancheng, there are many prostitutes, so there is a saying, "When you arrive in Yu Hua, your heart is open, when you arrive in Yancheng, you don't want to go home." Taking Yancheng as an example, it is said that there are no less than 200 households. Usually, they do not dress up and go out to sell their charm; those who want to inquire are reported with wine, and then they can stay with the Kun. The Rouge from the North is different from the Golden Powder of the Southern Dynasties.

There is a town in the south of Yancheng called Biancang, which is famous for its dead branches and peonies. Jinghua Yuan's book also mentions this matter. However, what is said is slightly different from the Yancheng County Chronicles. The County Chronicles roughly say: At the end of the Yuan Dynasty, Bian Yuanheng entered Zhang Shicheng's curtain and made many contributions. When Shicheng was defeated, he lived in seclusion in Yandu Biancang. Emperor Taizu of Ming Dynasty called him but he did not come out. In anger, he left him to guard Liaodong. Before leaving, he poured wine on the peony planted by his hand and said, "Wait for me to return south, and the flowers will bloom again." Since then, they have not contained buds for ten years. One year, in the wind and snow, the flowers were extravagant, and Yuanheng was pardoned and returned. Later, they were stolen by the salt envoy and planted in the official residence, and they withered and were abandoned. The Bian family picked up the dead ones and cultivated them to germinate again, and they became lush for a long time, so they were called dead branches and peonies. The colors are divided into red and white, and the area can be half an acre. Xia Zhirong's poem says, "Strange Bian's double pearl flowers, white as fragrant snow and red as morning glow," is also chanting this. Every year, on Guyu, people from all directions come to watch, and they are crowded and crowded, and they are prosperous for a while. In the spring of Yihai, Yu once went to enjoy it during the spare time of lecturing and recorded a poem: Where is the peony good? Biancang is in Huainan. Dead branches are famous for their stability, and their beauty is truly kingly. I also work for flowers during Guyu today. Now, in the spring of flowers and willows, the commander is about to arrive again. Will the elegant guests of Jiangnan come for a visit?

Seeking Wife Advertisement

— Li Qin

Losing a person necessitates posting several missing person advertisements, which seems to have become a fixed method for finding someone. Even the way these advertisements are written follows a certain pattern: a narrow, elongated piece of paper with two large characters written horizontally at the top, "尋人" (Seeking Person), and the character "人" (person) is written upside down as "人." Writing the character upside down involves elements of phonetics, psychology, hope, auspicious sayings, and so on. To put it more plainly, "人倒人到" (person upside down, person arrives), meaning that going out will bring good fortune. Although this kind of talk may seem naive and laughable, it is a "national custom" inherited from our Chinese history of five thousand years. Just as a Taoist priest uses a talisman to summon heavenly gods and generals to capture demons, such wonderful tales can all be categorized within this realm. Apart from the convention of writing the character "人" upside down, the remaining wording also follows a certain formula. For example, it begins by stating "今因走失××一口" (Now, due to the loss of one member of family ××). Then, it proceeds to describe the missing person's name, age, appearance, build, native place, accent, and the style and material of the clothing they were wearing when they disappeared. Finally, realizing that one's own search efforts may not be sufficient, it appeals to "仁人君子" (benevolent people and gentlemen) with an inquiring tone, saying, "如有知其下落，因而尋獲送到某地某處者：酬洋若干。" (If anyone knows their whereabouts and can find them and deliver them to such and such a place: a reward of so many foreign dollars will be offered). Offering a reward for finding someone is a matter of course. As the sages said, "君子喻於義，小人喻於利." (The gentleman understands righteousness; the petty man understands profit.) China is not a purely virtuous country like the one in "鏡花緣" (Flowers in the Mirror). The structure of society is formed by a mixed organization of both gentlemen and petty men. Therefore, if one relies on the great effort of others, one must consider the imbalance between obligation and right, and balance the heavy burden on a level playing field. Otherwise, which gentleman or petty man would help to bring it to fruition? This kind of attached condition can indeed be regarded as logical and consistent with social philosophy. Finally, closely following "酬洋若干" (a reward of so many foreign dollars), a special ending tag is added: "儲欵以待，决不食言" (Funds are reserved to await, and we will definitely not break our word). This ending tag is also very necessary and generous because, without it, people would not know that the legal tender in his pocket is 麥克麥克 (full of money). In short, this composition method is very meticulous and flawless. Since the initial inventor or creator passed down this archetype, when later generations encounter missing persons and need to write several missing person advertisements, they always follow the same pattern, imitating it exactly. No one dares to violate this rule. However, recently, I discovered that a friend named Dan Yang Yanling at a certain place unfortunately lost his wife. He didn't have legal tender to place an advertisement in the newspaper, so he copied old articles and wrote hundreds of "Seeking Wife Advertisements," posting them in the alleyways and streets of towns and villages in the surrounding areas. However, as soon as his "Seeking Wife Advertisement" was posted on any wall, it caused a sensation, attracting many people to stop and watch. This appeal lies in the composition of his "Seeking Wife Advertisement," which reverses the previous pattern. It can be said to be the first revolutionary shot since the advent of missing person advertisements, full of wit and a dignified demeanor reminiscent of Confucius being besieged in Chencai and still not ceasing his stringed instrument songs. Below is the original text of the "Seeking Wife Advertisement": "Mei Xia, my dear sister: Why did you leave and not return? Our old mother is worried and has fallen ill, and the children are crying from hunger and cold. I search everywhere during the day, and my intestines twist nine times at night. All the affairs at home are in a state of disarray. Since we got married, five years have passed in a flash. I have never treated you badly, yet you treat me like a fool. You go out to play every day, and come back late at night. Sometimes you spend the night out, claiming to be accompanying your sisters. What exactly is going on? I've been really unlucky! You are so hard-hearted, abandoning your family affairs. Although I work outside, I only earn eight dollars a month. Life is very difficult, and our finances are tight. Yesterday, my mother-in-law came to our house and wailed and shouted at me, demanding that I find you within three days. If I don't find you within the time limit, how will I explain myself? Otherwise, she will sue me, and it will truly be a matter of life and death. I hope you will change your mind, and return immediately upon seeing this letter! Do not be tempted by others, to avoid future regret. Think of the deep love between husband and wife, and the precious mirror can be reunited. I will definitely not investigate the past, and we will maintain our love for each other. I don't have the legal tender to publish an advertisement in the newspaper, so I can only speak on paper. If you still don't return, I will try to commit suicide. I hope you will have great compassion and not make things difficult for me any further! I hereby sincerely inform you, Mei Xia, my dear sister."

Bamboos After Rain

—

Dancing

— Hua Ling

"Dancing to save the country" may be a thing of the past, but this year's Shanghai can truly be called the "Year of Dancing." Generally speaking, the era of shouting slogans has passed, and we have entered the era of implementation.

"Dancing" involves a man embracing a woman, following the rhythm of the music, stepping forward and backward in a measured pace. This was originally a Western pastime. Some gentlemen who like to say "We have it in China too" claim that "dancing" existed in our country during the Second Dynasty. However, let's be clear, the ancient dances in our country never involved a man embracing a woman in that way, did they? Some people say that dancing is quite hygienic, a type of indoor exercise. However, I have seen people who are addicted to dancing become thin and pale, and mentally disturbed. I have never seen anyone extend their life and cure illnesses through dancing. Fearing that relying on dancing to improve health is like taking opium every day to cure illness, it's a bit like that.

Westerners regard dancing as a form of social interaction, a refined form of entertainment. Naturally, "We have it in China too." Don't you see that tea dances are held to welcome and send off foreign guests? However, dancing is not necessarily absolutely refined in foreign countries either. Dancers in New York, Paris, and other places are always so tempting. We have that in China too, of course. Where? In small dance halls where one dollar buys eight, ten, or even twelve dances. There, it is full of the colors found in nightclubs in places like New York and Paris.

One dollar for ten, even twelve dances, can be said to have exhausted the possibilities of "cheap prices." But business is really difficult to do these days, and dance hall owners are no exception. Because shrewd dance patrons are bringing in dance partners they hired at even cheaper prices, the dance girls are sitting all night in "matchmaking shops," earning nothing, and quietly facing the non-dancers who are asking for a cup of plain water and setting up "character-splitting stalls" from beginning to end. Suppliers and consumers, those who have too much and those who are left over, perhaps economists can find a lot to analyze in this. However, the reality tells us that dance hall owners are all frowning and sighing, even though this year is a fully-fledged "Year of Dancing."

Statement

We have received a letter from Mr. A Yuan, stating that the "Water Lily" article by Qi Dong, published on March 4th in the "A Spring of Leisure Spent Admiring Flowers" special page, was actually plagiarized from his old work previously published in another newspaper. Such literary thieves are truly detestable. We do not know who Qi Dong is, and in addition to canceling his compensation, we will also impose a reputational penalty. This statement is made to this effect.

Swapping the Phoenix in the Nest

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Prologue: Appreciating Chrysanthemums Near the Double Ninth Festival for a Secluded Gathering, Stringing Pearls Revisits Old Dreams, Drinking Hatred for a Thousand Autumns

Lan Chang raised his teacup to me and said with a smile, "Have a bowl of tea first, then read the documents. Don't start guessing before you see them. If you're so nervous, everyone I've invited today will become characters in a book." Hearing him say this made me feel like I was overthinking things, so I followed his advice, calmed myself down, took a few sips of tea, and then opened the cloth package. Inside, I found three thick notebooks. The notebooks had blue cloth covers and yellow silk bookmarks, with the words "含悲集" (Collection of Sorrow) written on them. I flipped through all three books and found that they were all handwritten in very elegant cursive script. There were diaries, poems, letters, and even bills, all completely unorganized manuscripts. These manuscripts were about someone's life, that much could be said. However, one couldn't make heads or tails of this kind of writing by glancing at it, so I had to put it down. There was also a stack of Xuan paper poetry slips with vermilion silk grids, some with antique-style bronze cauldron patterns printed on them. The slips were also written in a very flowing Su style. The title at the top of the slip read "石點館新聯珠" (New Linked Pearls of the Stone Dot Pavilion), followed by "惜玉外史戲擬" (Jaded Historian's Playful Imitation). I said, "These poetry slips are also from another person's hand. What's going on?" Lan Chang said, "Ah! Yes. Mr. Ruan said that there are twenty-four Linked Pearls in these documents. Just read through these Linked Pearls once, and you'll understand." So I moved the poetry slips to the middle of the tea table, dragged my chair next to Lan Chang, and we both looked at them together. Each Linked Pearl was marked with a number, so I looked at the first one:

"蓋聞蘭生空谷，流泉度其孤芳，月落秋階，蒼鶴憐其皓魄。是以高山一曲，焦桐託生死之交．落花無言，巾車感相逢之晚。"

"It is said that orchids grow in empty valleys, and flowing springs nurture their solitary fragrance. The moon sets on autumn steps, and gray cranes pity their bright souls. Therefore, a tune from a high mountain expresses a friendship that transcends life and death, and fallen flowers are silent, as the curtained carriage feels the lateness of their meeting."

I nodded and said, "Okay, this is talking about the beginning of a friendship between two people. But it already has a sad tone at the beginning." Lan Chang said, "Don't interrupt yet. Keep reading." So I opened the second poetry slip and read the second poem.

"蓋聞二南之叶，好逮爲往晢所不能諱言。三問之辭，鐘情亦騷人所有以自託。故銅溝流翠，有緣得葉上之詩，彩鳳求凰，憐才悟零中之意。"

"It is said that the harmony of the Two Nans cannot be concealed by even the wise men of the past. The words of the Three Questions express affections that the poets also use to confide in. Therefore, in the Bronze Ditch, there is a chance to receive poems on leaves, and the colorful phoenix seeks its mate, understanding the meaning within the droplets."

"蓋聞春風巷陌，絲柳情長。烟雨江頭，盡樓夢冷……"

"It is said that in the spring breeze alleys, the silk willows are full of emotion. At the misty riverside, the dreams in the towers are cold..."

When I saw the eight characters below, I found them a bit difficult to understand, so I couldn't help but prop my hand under my chin and think deeply. Unexpectedly, at this time, Lan Chang didn't notice me and had already read several more poems. I stopped speculating and continued reading downwards, to the eighth poem.

"蓋聞求三年之艾，雖扁鵲莫起沉疴。索十萬之錢，是天孫允須重聘。故灰盡万心，商女不知亡國恨。撑將淚眼，落花猶似　樓人。（九）"

"It is said that seeking wormwood that is three years old, even Bian Que cannot cure a persistent illness. Demanding a hundred thousand coins is what the Heavenly Grandson surely needs for a second betrothal. Therefore, all hearts are reduced to ashes, and the singing girl does not know the hatred of the fallen kingdom. Straining tearful eyes, the falling flowers still resemble people in the tower. (9)"

Municipal Education Bureau Announces Elementary School Joint Sports Meet, Competition Guidelines, and Selection Rules for Callisthenics Teaching Materials

The regulations for the Municipal Education Bureau's Eighth Elementary School Joint Sports Meet have been published in yesterday's newspaper. The competition guidelines, callisthenics teaching materials, organizational rules for preliminary selection meetings, and guidelines for participating in group exercises will be continued below. (Note: The previously announced Elementary School Joint Sports Meet was the Seventh, but according to the Municipal Government's intention, last year's was the Seventh District Elementary School Joint Sports Meet. This year's should still be continuously named, so it is corrected to the Eighth.)

Joint Sports Meet Competition Guidelines

Male and female track and field athletes are generally divided into two groups, A, B, and C. (For the grouping standards, see yesterday's regulations.) Male and female athletes in Group B must be re-weighed before participating in each sports competition. Male and female athletes from each district must wear spiked running shoes for Group A track and field events. All other groups must wear ordinary running shoes. If an athlete competes in one group for a certain event, they cannot move up or down to any other group for another event. If such a situation is discovered, all points earned by the athlete will be canceled. Any athlete who engages in immoral behavior will be immediately disqualified. Any athlete who engages in unethical behavior on the field will be immediately disqualified from the competition. All athletes must wear the designated number (matching the one specified on the order list) on both the chest and back. The order of each race will be determined by a draw conducted by the organizing committee. The starting position or running line for each track athlete will be determined by a draw. Athletes in each field event should attempt to jump or throw in the order determined by the organizing committee. If the number of participants in each event is too large to compete in one session, preliminary and semi-final heats should be held before the final. Athletes who have already forfeited their right to compete may not rejoin the competition. There must be at least eight athletes in the final. If this is not possible in reality, this rule does not apply. At least two athletes should be selected from each group in the preliminary and semi-final heats. Athletes participating in both field and track events must obtain permission from the field event judges before attempting to jump or throw out of the prescribed order. If a track athlete intentionally pushes or obstructs another athlete's progress, whether it occurs in the preliminary, semi-final, or final, their qualifying status will be canceled. Athletes must not use equipment or other stimulants to enhance their performance and gain an unfair advantage. If the scores of each event are the same, the tied athletes will compete again, jumping or throwing higher or further until a winner is determined. The attire of the athletes will be determined by each district, and must be clean and elegant. If athletes have any protests, they must submit them in writing within one hour of the incident, along with a deposit of five yuan, to the appeals committee for review and decision. If the appeals committee believes that the protest is without sufficient grounds, the deposit will be forfeited. The protest letter must be signed and sealed by the chairman of the athlete's district selection committee. The decision of the appeals committee on the protest letter is final and cannot be appealed further.

Organizational Rules for Preliminary Selection Meetings

Organizational Rules for Preliminary Selection Meetings in Each District, Article 1: This meeting is organized to prepare for and select representatives to participate in the Municipal Private Elementary Schools' Eighth Joint Sports Meet. A district preliminary selection meeting is organized to be responsible for implementation. Article 2: The chairman of this meeting will be appointed by the Education Bureau. Four to six preparation personnel will be recommended by the chairman and submitted to the Education Bureau for approval and appointment. Article 3: For the convenience of preparation, this meeting may be divided into groups to handle various affairs. Article 4: The number of representatives from this district must not exceed the items and quantities stipulated by the Education Bureau, but in consideration of the expenses of this meeting, the number of representatives may be reduced as appropriate. Article 5: All expenses for this meeting to hold preliminary selections and participate in the Eighth Elementary School Joint Sports Meet, etc., will be covered by the Education Bureau's subsidies. Any shortfall will be shared by the schools in this district. Article 6: The expenses for athletes from each school in this district who register for group exercises will be borne by the schools themselves. Article 7: The date and location of the preliminary selection meeting in this district will be determined. Article 8: This meeting will be attached to a certain school. Article 9: This meeting will be dissolved upon the closing of the Eighth Elementary School Joint Sports Meet. Article 10: If there are any matters not covered in these rules, the Education Bureau shall amend them. Article 11: These rules shall be implemented from the date of promulgation by the Education Bureau.

Group Exercises Participation Guidelines

Group Exercises Participation Guidelines: Except for schools in the districts of Hu Nan, Zhabei, and the Special District, which must have at least one section participating, other districts may consider participation based on the circumstances of the schools. At least 60% of the students in each school must participate in the group exercises. The group exercises will showcase all of the usual callisthenics teaching materials. Each section must not exceed twenty minutes in time. The sports equipment and musical instruments used in the group exercises must be provided by each school. The schools must transport and set up the equipment on the field before the performance. The organizing committee will not be responsible. For the group exercises performance items, please prepare cards (one for each item) with the school name, title, and name of the physical education teacher, and submit them to the group exercises judges upon entry. The organizing committee will follow the order listed on the order list. If there are any changes to the various competitions, the chief referee will notify the reporters to make temporary announcements.

Joint Sports Meet Callisthenics Teaching Materials

Section 1 (Upper Limb Exercise) Preparation: Standing upright. Movements: Arms extended to the sides, hands raised. Arms extended to the sides, raised upwards. Arms lowered to the sides, return to the original posture. Arms lowered downwards. Repeat the exercises up to thirty-two beats, then stop. Section 2 (Four Limb Exercise) Preparation: Standing upright. Movements: Arms raised horizontally. Half-squat while simultaneously lowering both arms backward and diagonally downwards. Return to the previous posture. Restore the original preparatory posture. Repeat the exercises up to thirty-two beats, then stop. Section 3 (Waist Exercise) Preparation: Standing upright. Movements: Hands on hips, simultaneously step left foot to the side in a lunge. Upper body leans to the left. Return to the previous posture. Restore. Step right foot to the side in a lunge. Repeat the exercises up to thirty-two beats, then stop. Section 4 (Abdominal Exercise) Preparation: Standing upright. Movements: Arms raised forward and upwards. Upper body leans forward, simultaneously lowering both arms forward and downwards, forming a diagonally upwards posture. Return to the previous posture. Arms lowered downwards. Repeat the exercises up to thirty-two beats, then stop. Section 5 (Fast Exercise) Preparation: Standing upright. Movements: Arms extended to the sides, raised upwards. Clap hands while simultaneously jumping open-legged. Arms lowered to the sides while simultaneously jumping back to a closed-legged stance. Repeat the exercises up to thirty-two beats, then stop. (Movements should not be too fast.) Section 6 (Breathing Exercise) Preparation: Standing upright. Movements: Arms raised forward horizontally (inhale). Arms bent at the chest, palms pressing against the chest (forceful inhale). Arms returned to the previous posture (exhale). Arms returned to the original position (forceful exhale). Repeat the exercises up to sixteen beats, then stop.

Education News

The Siamese Government Inflicts New Harsh Regulations on Overseas Chinese Education: No Chinese Language Teaching Allowed Outside of Class; Chinese Textbooks Must Be Submitted for Review

In recent years, the Siamese government's various harsh regulations to undermine overseas Chinese education have been frequently reported in Shanghai and Guangdong newspapers. Recently, the country has intensified its efforts, not only oppressing Chinese children residing in the country to study Siamese language step by step, but also prohibiting Chinese people from studying their motherland's literature outside of class time. This new regulation is scheduled to take effect on the Buddhist calendar's New Year's Day (i.e., April 1st of the Gregorian calendar). All levels of overseas Chinese schools are currently fighting for reason, but based on the failure of previous petitions, it can be concluded that this new harsh regulation is bound to be implemented. The contents of the new harsh regulation are summarized as follows:

Since the Siamese government promulgated the so-called Compulsory Education Ordinance the year before last, all Chinese children residing in the country must study Siamese language. Although overseas Chinese compatriots unanimously opposed it at the time, they were isolated and helpless, and ultimately failed. Afterwards, the Chinese people stopped running schools one after another, or were unreasonably closed down by the Siamese government. The few remaining schools have also been changed to teach Siamese language, which is the so-called compulsory education class. Only a small number of Chinese children who exceed the age limit stipulated by the country can be taught Chinese. As for Chinese children receiving compulsory education, although there is a provision for teaching Chinese for five or six hours per week, the time is too short to be sufficient for distribution. Requests to increase the time have been denied by the Siamese government. As a last resort, each Chinese school can only hold classes in the morning and after school in the afternoon (Siamese schools usually dismiss after 3:00 PM due to the hot weather), and teach Chinese for a certain amount of time to make up for it. Unexpectedly, this method of last resort stipulates that in addition to Siamese language, required subjects such as self-cultivation, arithmetic, general knowledge, hygiene, drawing, and scouts must still use Siamese textbooks. From the first to second grades, there are five hours and twenty minutes per week for elective subjects. For the fourth and fifth grades, there are ten hours and twenty minutes per week for elective subjects (the Siamese school system graduates in five years). During this elective subject time, English, French, or Chinese can be selected. The class time is stipulated to be from 9:00 AM to 2:00 PM. It is not allowed to extend the time before class or after school, and the elective textbooks (referring to Chinese textbooks) must be sent to the country's Ministry of Education for review and approval before they can be used. On the surface, this new regulation seems to be beneficial to the Chinese, because the time for teaching Chinese in the fourth and fifth grades has slightly increased compared to the past. However, in reality, it is counterproductive in terms of writing skills, because the time for teaching Chinese cannot be increased outside of class.

The National Postal Workers' Union Founds the China Postal Workers' Correspondence School

The standing committee of the National Postal Workers' Union resolved to establish the China Postal Workers' Correspondence School to improve postal workers' intelligence and cultivate postal talents. Preparations began in May of last year and have been largely completed after nearly a year. Lu Jingshi, Zhu Xuefan, Zhao Shusheng, Zhang Kechang, Wang Yisheng, Cao Jiaxiu, Zhu Yinghua, Chen Shi, and Wei De were appointed as school directors, and advanced figures in the transportation sector were hired as honorary school directors. The curriculum is divided into advanced and elementary classes. The elementary class is equivalent to the junior high school level, and the advanced class is equivalent to the senior high school level. Each class offers six subjects: Chinese, English, mathematics, geography, history, and postal knowledge. The lecture notes for each subject have been edited in cooperation with experts in each subject and postal bureau colleagues. The qualifications for admission are that the applicant must be: 1. A colleague serving in the postal bureau; 2. A relative or friend of a colleague in the postal bureau who is introduced by the colleague; 3. No restrictions on gender or age.

Rejuvenating the Nation and Rescuing Homeless Children (I)

— Lei Zhen

Broadcast Speech by the National Children's Year Implementation Committee

Today, I am here to discuss the issue of rejuvenating the nation and rescuing homeless children with you. Children today are the backbone of the nation's future and the masters of the country's future. Everyone knows this, so there is no need to waste words explaining it. A person's lifelong habits, personality, character, and hobbies are all developed in childhood. Therefore, for an individual, the cultivation of childhood is the foundation of one's life. For a nation and a country, children's education is the foundation of the nation's rise and fall. Since our nation and country inherited the weakness and poverty of the late Qing Dynasty, the Republic of China has been established for more than 20 years. Social order has not been stabilized, politics cannot be clarified, academic studies cannot progress, and rural areas have gone bankrupt, commerce has stagnated, and various industries have declined. The crux of this disease is certainly not a single cause, but the past neglect of children's education is indeed one of the main reasons. It must be understood that if a person develops bad habits such as selfishness, greed, laziness, and shamelessness in childhood, they will become a bad element of society when they grow up. Therefore, today's bandits, corrupt officials, and swindlers are mostly bad children of yesteryear. Therefore, to rejuvenate the nation, we must catch up in children's education with great haste.

Now, let us try to explore the situation of children's education in our country. According to the Ministry of Education's survey in the 21st year of the Republic of China, the number of school-age children in our country is 49,688,917. Among these more than 49 million school-age children, only 11,923,066 are in school. The number of children out of school is 37,465,851. Let us try to calculate: the number of children out of school exceeds the number of children in school by more than three times. We do not need to discuss the education situation of children in school now. What we want to discuss now is why there are so many children out of school. Based on my observations, there are roughly three reasons for children being out of school:

The first reason is that the supply of elementary school facilities does not meet the demand. According to the Ministry of Education's statistics in the 21st year of the Republic of China, the number of elementary schools in the country is 260,437, and they are mostly distributed in urban areas. Because elementary schools cannot accommodate all school-age children, some children are out of school because they have nowhere to study. This kind of out-of-school situation is unavoidable. Regarding this point, education is actively seeking methods, practicing compulsory education, increasing the number of elementary schools, and expanding the capacity of existing elementary schools. This year, due to the implementation of the short-term compulsory education in the National Children's Year, the number of children attending school can be increased by 4 million. It is expected that after five years, 70 to 80 percent of school-age children will have the opportunity to attend school.

The second reason is the stubborn mentality of children's parents. Under the conditions of the patriarchal society in the past, Chinese people considered their children to be descendants of the family and did not recognize that their children were small citizens of the country. As the saying goes, "People leave children and grass leaves roots." Therefore, parents are mostly only willing to raise their children to adulthood and do not think about teaching them to become useful citizens of the country. The children of those with property indulge in extravagant lives all year round, regardless of the adverse effects they will have on society in the future. The children of those without property are engaged in farming or hard labor with their parents and do not think about letting them go to school and become literate. There are many cases of children being out of school because of this. After the implementation of compulsory education in the future, forced enrollment will reduce the number of children out of school.

The third reason is the problem of homeless children that we are afraid to handle. These homeless children are the most neglected by today's society and the most harmful to future society, as they are children who are out of school and lack care. Nowadays, we can often see many beggar children in cities or towns, living like wild animals, picking coal, picking up rags, begging for leftovers, and stealing firewood. During the day, they fight by the garbage dumps, and at night, they lie down by the stoves of small shops. Some of these children are orphans without parents, and some are the children of disaster victims after rural bankruptcy. These children are generally seen as worse than pigs and dogs, and suffer the contempt and abuse of society. They do not receive the edification of knowledge, nor do they seek the skills of a profession. After growing up, they have nowhere to turn and become bandits and accomplices. In particular, because they have suffered the misfortune of humanity in their childhood, they have developed a cold and shameless mentality. Therefore, these children, after growing up, either become bandits or cruel murderers. If they become spies, they are shameless and cunning thieves. Because they have no scruples about life, they are not afraid of national law, do not fear human words, do not know morality, and do not care about integrity. Punishment is not enough to scare them, and propriety and righteousness are not enough to restrain them. From a positive perspective, we do not know how many promising talents have been buried and how many useful citizens have been abandoned among these homeless children. From a negative perspective, disrupting national security and endangering national survival are all done by these uneducated people. From this point of view, if we want to rejuvenate the nation, we must actively discuss ways to rescue homeless children.

Let us now try to consider the existing organizations for rescuing homeless children in our country. The only organization for rescuing homeless children now is the orphanage. According to the Ministry of Education's statistics in the 22nd year, there are six provincial and municipal orphanages in the country, 95 county and municipal orphanages, and 57 private orphanages. In total, there are only 158 orphanages in the country, accommodating only 15,772 children. Think about it, there are more than 37.4 million out-of-school children in our country. The number of homeless children among the out-of-school children is probably more than 10,000 in one city alone. In this sense, the orphanages in the country are not enough to accommodate the homeless children in one city. Such rescue is really too inadequate. Although we are actively promoting compulsory education now, compulsory education can only rescue children who are out of school. It still has no power to rescue homeless children, because compulsory education is only responsible for teaching and not responsible for care. Rescuing homeless children requires both teaching and care, and also requires finding a way out for the children when they grow up. Therefore, we must find another way to rescue homeless children.

National Products Special Issue

A Word of Contribution

Cooperation between the National Products Industry and the Political World

— Yang An

Yesterday, the China National Industry and Foreign Trade Association and the China National Products Production and Marketing Cooperation Association hosted a public banquet at the Bank Club for Mr. Wu Daquan, Minister of Industry. In addition to the factory inspection specialists from the Executive Yuan, the attendees were also leading figures in Shanghai's industrial sector and powerful members engaged in the national products business. The administrative and industrial/commercial sectors gathered together to express their opinions on improving industry and to address the hardships of factories. It was like a family reunion, direct and without secrets, which seemed to foster a sense of camaraderie and represented a situation unseen for over a decade. Mr. Wu stated that he greatly admired the fact that various factories were able to seek progress on their own under the circumstances of foreign goods dumping and a sluggish market. He noted that all of their products were improving with each passing day, demonstrating the potential to surpass foreign-made goods. However, he also noted that in the development of business, it is better to rely on one's own strength rather than depend on others. The national products industry should strive for self-reliance, improve itself, and seek excellence, so that domestic goods will naturally be used and enjoyed by the people. There is no need to force or persuade people to do so. Currently, the national products industry should avoid engaging in meaningless competition or producing substandard goods to devalue national products. Instead, it should focus on improving technology, lowering costs, and improving efficiency. The driving force behind encouraging the people to love national products lies within the national products industry itself. How to achieve production and marketing cooperation to extend to the entire nation and abroad also lies within the industrial sector itself. China's mechanical industry is still in its infancy. It may be beneficial to adopt the transitional method of "welcoming foreign goods for production tools, while using domestically produced goods for consumer items." In the future, self-sufficiency will rely even more on the efforts of the national products industry. During the banquet, the industrial sector representatives expressed the hope that the raw material tax would be refunded to demonstrate encouragement. They also stated that trade association organizations should be strengthened without compromise. The establishment of industries in various provinces should be coordinated to consider the overall situation, to have a comprehensive plan, to avoid duplication and prevent partiality. They concluded by emphasizing the need to exchange opinions and coordinate with each other at any time, and that discussions of certain issues could be conducted with government officials to mutually express opinions and to eliminate past misunderstandings and meaningless bureaucracy. This spirit of unity between government and people portends unlimited hope for the national products industry. Since taking office as minister, Mr. Wu has worked hard to support the national products industry by establishing commercial officials abroad, organizing the Agricultural Foundation Bureau, and sending personnel to investigate local industries. He has provided convenience for the development of China's industry in every way. In the future, there will be many more opportunities for administrative and industrial sectors to work together. This inaugural gathering promises to fulfill many aspirations and to serve as a test for future development.

Shen Bao Local Supplement - Idle Talk - Hunan Plans to Establish a Prostitute School by Jiawei. This may be a commendable thing. Our society today is indeed in constant "construction" and "improvement"! Isn't that right? What "economic construction," "aviation construction," "national defense construction," "XX construction," and even "thrift movement," "mother education movement," "local goods movement," "XX movement"..., many, many grandly said to be "planning" to reform today's society and country through "construction" and "movement"!

Indeed, although we haven't clearly seen the effects and results of these examples, under the authorities' "painstaking" advocacy and promotion, perhaps they can temporarily give people some excitement and stimulation?

In today's newspaper, we found another example. According to reports - Hunan Provincial Games Association plans to open a prostitute school, planning to accommodate 500 people. They will be taught embroidery, sewing, and various handicrafts, as well as practical subjects such as Mandarin and abacus. Registration will be carried out first. After registration, the prostitutes will take an exam, and based on the exam results, they will be divided into classes for training according to their level. The graduation period is at most two years and at least one year; the daily course is six hours, just like a regular school. After one class graduates, those who register later will be enrolled for training. It is said that this plan is currently being prepared and is expected to be realized in the autumn of this year.

Originally, we still remember that not long ago, prostitutes and dancers wanted to enter school but could not find a way; even more so, children whose mothers sold their bodies for a living were rejected by the school authorities. Their reason was: because they wanted to prevent the corruption of other "good family children," and were even more afraid of affecting the school's reputation. However, whether these "reasons" have a factual basis is still questionable; but here it fully reflects the morbidity of our old society and the social psychology of some people! Therefore, today, in Hunan, the establishment of a school dedicated to educating prostitutes who have been discriminated against and abandoned is undoubtedly a somewhat satisfactory thing!

However, what we have seen in the past from various local authorities, so-called "abolition of prostitution," "prohibition of prostitution," and even "public prostitution," etc., those disguised taxation methods of "imposing taxes in the name of prohibition" are, on the contrary, increasing the burden and suffering of prostitutes, and never finding a correct way out!

Therefore, today's Hunan authorities' "prostitute school" can indeed be said to be a new face in the sound of "abolition of prostitution"!

However, we have to say it again, under such a method of "not eradicating the roots," under the current environment, can we receive its expected effects?

Carpenter's Son by Yan A pretentious act that made his companions laugh. Although Little Flower's dad's face turned red, he was extremely happy in his heart: Little Flower will graduate in another year!

Little Flower is really too smart and hardworking. It seems that he was born with something more than his classmates. Even extracurricular questions, he can answer them all. When he gets home, he always does his homework at his small desk, waiting for his dad to come back to eat dinner together. But today, when Dad came back, he didn't see Little Flower. He asked Mom, who said he came home early. This house, besides the front door facing the street, has a back door leading to the riverbank. But Dad opened the back door and called Little Flower's name, but no one answered. The sky was about to turn completely dark, and there was still some light reflecting from the river. Dad turned on his flashlight and looked around. There was a dark shadow sitting under the roots of a tree by the river, wearing a glorious uniform, the uniform of the county elementary school! So the carpenter dad ran over. When he picked up his son, he saw clear tears welling up in his son's eyes. This had never happened before. His son had told stories from books, saying that people shouldn't cry, and that no matter what difficulties they faced, they should cheer up and do it. So, why was this storytelling elementary school student crying?

Dad and Mom used many kind words to question their son. The son told the following:

A classmate lost a fountain pen. When the monitor came to check the classroom, the pen was found in my drawer. They all made faces and called me a thief. The principal took me to the teaching office and questioned me. I really didn't steal it. I don't know where the pen came from. The principal wants Dad to go to school with me tomorrow...

The carpenter dad jumped up. He knew his son would never steal anything. He wanted to go to the school immediately to question the principal. His son was going to graduate in another year! A graduate of a county elementary school is such a noble thing!

But he immediately remembered the story his son had told, that no matter what difficulties you face, you must cheer up and do it, and that people shouldn't cry! So he sat down again and patted his son's shoulder, asking in a low voice, "Tell Dad, did you really not steal that fountain pen?"

The son widened his eyes and stared at Dad, not understanding why Dad didn't believe his words.

Over there, under the light of the kerosene lamp, Mom's face was reflected, her eyebrows furrowed, biting her lower lip. Did she also suspect her son of being a thief?

The carpenter's son, Little Flower, burst into tears...

(End)

His broad chest and shoulders shook with laughter, and he comically stuck out his tongue, making all sorts of ugly and grotesque faces.

Feature - The Completion Ceremony of the Third Dock at the Jiangnan Shipyard by Yu. Yesterday afternoon, the weather was strangely gloomy, as if it was about to rain.

Many men and women in tattered clothes mixed in with the blue-cloth and gray-clothed workers'队伍, running into the tall gate of the "Jiangnan Shipyard of the Navy" with smiles: "The warship entering the dock today is very big!"

Perhaps they all lived near the shipyard and often went there to play, and ran very familiarly into the third dock.

Soon, these people who ran in thickened the line surrounding the dock, and the navy stood in front of them, blocking their advance.

The third dock was indeed very large, looking like a small lake. At both ends of the dock were two bridges, and the pontoon bridge near the Huangpu River was also a gate. The edges of the dock were steel plates, and the body was made of wood, trapezoidal in shape. They were all coated with black asphalt, perhaps not long ago, because the asphalt smell was still so strong.

Page 18

Bright national flags were hung around the dock. In the space in the middle of the dock, three red, white, and blue silk ribbons were hung horizontally with three tricolor red, white, and blue彩球s.

The pumping station was on the right side of the gate. There were five winches installed on both sides of the dock.

The stage, temporarily set up on the bridge inside, was very simple, with a portrait of Dr. Sun Yat-sen and two vases.

Gradually, a dozen or so naval officers gathered next to the stage. Their uniforms were all very smart, and the yellow handles of their command swords were held in white gloves, making them look even more majestic. Their hands frequently touched the brims of their hats.

At that moment, the gate, which was as high as the horizon, gradually floated up from under the water, rising four or five feet above the ground. Two iron cables secured the gate, and under the traction of two winches, the gate left its original position and leaned against the bank outside the gate in the Huangpu River.

A gasoline boat began to sail towards the Ninghai warship not far from the dock.

Here, the navy bugle next to the stage blew "lala", and the officers formed a team to the bridge and saluted according to the ritual.

The song was sung loudly and neatly by a team of elementary school students in blue cloth uniforms.

The workers in the dock also began to work, pushing the wood stacked next to the dock one by one into the water. They floated on木排s, using brooms as oars, working in the dock.

The small gasoline boat towed the "ceremonial ship entering the dock" Ninghai over. Some officers in neat uniforms stood on the bow of the ship. Closer, I saw that in addition to the officers and navy on the bow of the ship, there were also seven or eight ladies, one of whom was standing in the middle, wearing a white silk披肩, a white silk旗袍, and white leather shoes; holding a bouquet of鲜花 in her hand. Without anyone telling me, everyone knew that she was Miss Ma Mingye, who was there for the ribbon-cutting ceremony.

As the bow of the ship entered the dock entrance, the small and large边砲s next to the dock burst out with a rattling sound. Amidst the military music, the people watching on both sides were hit by碎边砲纸 falling from the sky, like a bride and groom.

The bow of the ship was about to touch the彩球s. The captain standing next to Miss Ma stretched out his hand and grabbed the彩球s. Miss Ma quickly cut the彩带 with the scissors in her white-gloved hand. The彩带 fell to both sides, and the彩球s fell onto the ship.

Miss Ma's brown face showed a hint of a smile, allowing several camera lenses to capture her smile from under the ship.

The Ninghai warship was towed by the iron cables on the winches on both sides, swaying into the dock. As the iron cables passed, the people on both sides were driven to the back. The foreman held a microphone and shouting, "Hurry up! Slow down!" to direct the workers.

In this way, the ship sailed until it was more than ten feet away from the bridge before it was settled. Miss Ma, the captain, and other officials standing on the bow of the ship retreated, and the officers on the bridge also retreated under the sound of military号s.

After having tea and snacks in the office, the expansion project of the third dock of the Jiangnan Shipyard of the Navy was completed at this time.

According to the news released by the shipyard: The shipyard originally had two dry docks, one over five hundred feet long and one over four hundred feet long, which could repair and build a large number of medium-sized warships and merchant ships of about 10,000 tons. After the expansion project of the third dock, the length is over six hundred and forty feet, the width is one hundred feet, and the depth is twenty-six feet. In the future, large ships from various countries coming to Shanghai can easily enter the dock for inspection.

On the way back, the rain was falling like tears again.
